69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
2 INTRODUCED BY V. RICCI
3
4 A BILL FOR AN ACT ENTITLED: “AN ACT GENERALLY REVISING THE UNIFORM COMMERCIAL CODE;
5 UPDATING TERMINOLOGY FOR THE DIGITAL AGE; PROVIDING RULES FOR TRANSACTIONS
6 INVOLVING CERTAIN DIGITAL ASSETS INCLUDING CRYPTOCURRENCY; PROHIBITING CENTRAL
7 BANK DIGITAL CURRENCY; AND AMENDING SECTIONS 30-1-101, 30-1-107, 30-1-201, 30-1-212, 30-1-301,
8 30-2-102, 30-2-106, 30-2-201, 30-2-202, 30-2-203, 30-2-205, 30-2-209, 30-2A-102, 30-2A-103, 30-2A-107, 30-
9 2A-201, 30-2A-202, 30-2A-203, 30-2A-205, 30-2A-208, 30-3-102, 30-3-104, 30-3-125, 30-3-401, 30-3-605, 30-
10 4A-103, 30-4A-105, 30-4A-201, 30-4A-202, 30-4A-203, 30-4A-207, 30-4A-208, 30-4A-210, 30-4A-211, 30-4A-
11 305, 30-5-124, 30-5-136, 30-7-102, 30-7-107, 30-8-112, 30-8-113, 30-8-116, 30-8-120, 30-8-333, 30-9A-102,
12 30-9A-104, 30-9A-105, 30-9A-203, 30-9A-204, 30-9A-207, 30-9A-208, 30-9A-209, 30-9A-210, 30-9A-301, 30-
13 9A-304, 30-9A-305, 30-9A-310, 30-9A-312, 30-9A-313, 30-9A-314, 30-9A-316, 30-9A-317, 30-9A-323, 30-9A-
14 324, 30-9A-330, 30-9A-331, 30-9A-332, 30-9A-334, 30-9A-341, 30-9A-404, 30-9A-406, 30-9A-408, 30-9A-509,
15 30-9A-513, 30-9A-601, 30-9A-605, 30-9A-608, 30-9A-611, 30-9A-613, 30-9A-614, 30-9A-615, 30-9A-616, 30-
16 9A-619, 30-9A-620, 30-9A-621, 30-9A-624, 30-9A-628, AND 71-3-125, MCA.”
17
18 WHEREAS, a central bank digital currency has been defined by the Federal Reserve as a digital form
19 of central bank money that is widely available to the general public; and
20 WHEREAS, central bank money refers to money that is a liability of the central bank and not of a
21 commercial bank; and
22 WHEREAS, countries around the world, including the United States, are evaluating whether or not to
23 issue and how to issue and operate a central bank digital currency; and
24 WHEREAS, a central bank digital currency would fundamentally reimagine our banking and financial
25 system by changing the relationship between citizens and the Federal Reserve; and
26 WHEREAS, a central bank digital currency would severely undermine financial privacy for citizens; and
27 WHEREAS, the availability of a central bank digital currency in the United States would undermine the
28 important role banks play in financial intermediation and limit credit availability because funds would move from
- 1 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 commercial banks to the Federal Reserve where they cannot be lent back into the economy; and
2 WHEREAS, a central bank digital currency would fundamentally rewire our banking and financial
3 system by changing the relationship between citizens and the Federal Reserve.
4
5 BE IT ENACTED BY THE LEGISLATURE OF THE STATE OF MONTANA:
6
7 Section 1. Section 30-1-101, MCA, is amended to read:
8 "30-1-101. Short titles -- scope of chapter. (1) Chapters 1 through 9A and [sections 94 through 109]
9 of this title may be cited as Uniform Commercial Code.
10 (2) As used in chapters 1 through 9A and [sections 94 through 109] of this title "code" means
11 "Uniform Commercial Code" unless the context indicates otherwise.
12 (3) This chapter may be cited as the Uniform Commercial Code--General Provisions.
13 (4) This chapter applies to a transaction to the extent that it is governed by chapters 2 through 5,
14 7, 8, and 9A, and [sections 94 through 109] of this title.
15 (5) Nothing in chapters 1 through 9A and [sections 94 through 109] of this title may be construed to
16 support, endorse, create, or implement a national digital currency."
17
18 Section 2. Section 30-1-107, MCA, is amended to read:
19 "30-1-107. Waiver or renunciation of claim or right after breach. A claim or right arising out of an
20 alleged breach may be discharged in whole or in part without consideration by agreement of the aggrieved
21 party in an authenticated a signed record."
22
23 Section 3. Section 30-1-201, MCA, is amended to read:
24 "30-1-201. General definitions. (1) Unless the context requires otherwise, words or phrases defined
25 in this section, or in the additional definitions contained in other chapters of the code that apply to particular
26 chapters or parts of chapters, have the meanings stated.
27 (2) Subject to additional definitions contained in other chapters of this code that apply to specific
28 chapters or parts of chapters:
- 2 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 (a) "Action" in the sense of a judicial proceeding includes recoupment, counterclaim, setoff, suit in
2 equity, and any other proceeding in which rights are determined.
3 (b) "Aggrieved party" means a party entitled to pursue a remedy.
4 (c) "Agreement" means the bargain of the parties in fact, as found in their language or inferred
5 from other circumstances, including course of performance, course of dealing, or usage of trade as provided in
6 30-1-205.
7 (d) "Authenticate" means to:
8 (i) sign; or
9 (ii) execute or adopt a symbol, or encrypt a record in whole or in part, with present intent to:
10 (A) identify the authenticating party; and
11 (B) adopt, accept, or establish the authenticity of a record or term.
12 (e) (d) "Bank" means any person engaged in the business of banking and includes a savings bank,
13 savings and loan association, credit union, and trust company.
14 (f) (e) "Bearer" means a person in control of a negotiable electronic document of title or a person in
15 possession of a negotiable instrument, negotiable tangible document of title, or certificated security payable to
16 bearer or endorsed in blank.
17 (g) (f) (i) "Bill of lading" means a document of title evidencing the receipt of goods for shipment issued
18 by a person engaged in the business of directly or indirectly transporting or forwarding goods.
19 (ii) The term does not include a warehouse receipt.
20 (h) (g) "Branch" includes a separately incorporated foreign branch of a bank.
21 (i) (h) "Burden of establishing" a fact means the burden of persuading the trier of fact that the
22 existence of the fact is more probable than its nonexistence.
23 (j) (i) "Buyer in ordinary course of business" means a person that buys goods, in good faith, without
24 knowledge that the sale violates the rights of another person in the goods, and in the ordinary course from a
25 person, other than a pawnbroker, in the business of selling goods of that kind. A person buys goods in the
26 ordinary course if the sale to the person comports with the usual or customary practices in the kind of business
27 in which the seller is engaged or with the seller's own usual or customary practices. A person that sells oil, gas,
28 or other minerals at the wellhead or minehead is a person in the business of selling goods of that kind. A buyer
- 3 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 in ordinary course of business may buy for cash, by exchange of other property, or on secured or unsecured
2 credit, and may acquire goods or documents of title under a preexisting contract for sale. Only a buyer that
3 takes possession of the goods or has a right to recover the goods from the seller under chapter 2 may be a
4 buyer in ordinary course of business. A person that acquires goods in a transfer in bulk or as security for or in
5 total or partial satisfaction of a money debt is not a buyer in ordinary course of business.
6 (k) (j) "Conspicuous", with reference to a term, means so written, displayed, or presented that, based
7 on the totality of the circumstances, a reasonable person against which it is to operate ought to have noticed it.
8 Whether a term is "conspicuous" or not is for decision by the court. Conspicuous terms include the following:
9 (i) a heading in capitals equal to or greater in size than the surrounding text, or in contrasting type,
10 font, or color to the surrounding text of the same or lesser size; and
11 (ii) language in the body of a record or display in larger type than the surrounding text, or in
12 contrasting type, font, or color to the surrounding text of the same size, or set off from surrounding text of the
13 same size by symbols or other marks that call attention to the language.
14 (l) (k) "Consumer" means an individual who enters into a transaction primarily for personal, family, or
15 household purposes.
16 (m) (l) "Contract" means the total legal obligation that results from the parties' agreement as affected
17 by this code and as supplemented by any other applicable rules of law.
18 (n) (m) "Creditor" includes a general creditor, a secured creditor, a lien creditor, and any representative
19 of creditors, including an assignee for the benefit of creditors, a trustee in bankruptcy, a receiver in equity, and
20 an executor or administrator of an insolvent debtor's or assignor's estate.
21 (o) (n) "Defendant" includes a person in the position of defendant in a counterclaim or third-party
22 claim.
23 (p) (o) "Delivery" with respect to an electronic document of title means voluntary transfer of control
24 and, with respect to instruments, tangible documents of title, or an instrument, a tangible document of title, or
25 an authoritative tangible copy of a record evidencing chattel paper, means voluntary transfer of possession.
26 (q) (p) (i) "Document of title" means a record:
27 (A) that in the regular course of business or financing is treated as adequately evidencing that the
28 person in possession or control of the record is entitled to receive, control, hold, and dispose of the record and
- 4 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 the goods the record covers; and
2 (B) that purports to be issued by or addressed to a bailee and to cover goods in the bailee's
3 possession which are either identified or are fungible portions of an identified mass.
4 (ii) The term includes a bill of lading, transport document, dock warrant, dock receipt, warehouse
5 receipt, and order for delivery of goods. An electronic document of title is evidenced by a record consisting of
6 information stored in an electronic medium. A tangible document of title is evidenced by a record consisting of
7 information that is inscribed on a tangible medium.
8 (q) “Electronic” means relating to technology having electrical, digital, magnetic, wireless, optical,
9 electromagnetic, or similar capabilities.
10 (r) "Fault" means wrongful act, omission, breach, or default.
11 (s) "Fungible goods" means:
12 (i) goods of which any unit, by nature or usage of trade, is the equivalent of any other like unit; or
13 (ii) goods which by agreement are treated as equivalent.
14 (t) "Genuine" means free of forgery or counterfeiting.
15 (u) "Good faith", except as otherwise provided in chapter 5, means honesty in fact and the
16 observance of reasonable commercial standards of fair dealing.
17 (v) "Holder" means:
18 (i) the person in possession of a negotiable instrument that is payable either to bearer or to an
19 identified person that is the person in possession;
20 (ii) a the person in possession of a negotiable tangible document of title if the goods are
21 deliverable either to bearer or to the order of the person in possession; or
22 (iii) a the person in control, other than pursuant to 30-7-107(7) of a negotiable electronic document
23 of title.
24 (w) "Insolvency proceedings" includes an assignment for the benefit of creditors or other
25 proceeding intended to liquidate or rehabilitate the estate of the person involved.
26 (x) "Insolvent" means:
27 (i) having generally ceased to pay debts in the ordinary course of business other than as a result
28 of bona fide dispute;
- 5 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 (ii) unable to pay debts as they become due; or
2 (iii) insolvent within the meaning of the federal bankruptcy law.
3 (y) "Money" means a medium of exchange that is currently authorized or adopted by a domestic or
4 foreign government and is not in an electronic form. The term includes a monetary unit of account established
5 by an intergovernmental organization or by pursuant to an agreement between two or more countries.
6 (z) "Organization" means a person other than an individual.
7 (aa) "Party", as distinct from "third party", means a person that has engaged in a transaction or
8 made an agreement subject to this code.
9 (bb) "Person" means an individual, corporation, business trust, estate, trust, partnership, limited
10 liability company, association, joint venture, government, governmental subdivision, agency, or instrumentality,
11 public corporation, or any other legal or commercial entity. The term includes a protected series, however
12 denominated, of an entity if the protected series is established under law other than this code that limits, or
13 limits if conditions specified under the law are satisfied, the ability of a creditor of the entity or of any other
14 protected series of the entity to satisfy a claim from assets of the protected series.
15 (cc) "Presumption" or "presumed" means that the trier of fact must find the existence of the fact
16 presumed unless and until evidence is introduced which would support a finding of its nonexistence.
17 (dd) "Purchase" means taking by sale, lease, discount, negotiation, mortgage, pledge, lien, security
18 interest, issue or reissue, gift, or any other voluntary transaction creating an interest in property.
19 (ee) "Purchaser" means a person that takes by purchase.
20 (ff) "Record" means information that is inscribed on a tangible medium or that is stored in an
21 electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form.
22 (gg) "Remedy" means any remedial right to which an aggrieved party is entitled with or without
23 resort to a tribunal.
24 (hh) "Representative" means any other person empowered to act for another, including an agent, an
25 officer of a corporation or association, and a trustee, executor, or administrator of an estate.
26 (ii) "Right" includes a remedy.
27 (jj) "Security interest" means an interest in personal property or fixtures which secures payment or
28 performance of an obligation. The term also includes any interest of a consignor and a buyer of accounts,
- 6 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 chattel paper, a payment intangible, or a promissory note in a transaction that is subject to chapter 9A. The
2 special property interest of a buyer of goods on identification of those goods to a contract for sale under 30-2-
3 401 is not a "security interest", but a buyer may also acquire a "security interest" by complying with chapter 9A.
4 Except as otherwise provided in 30-2-505, the right of a seller or lessor of goods under chapter 2 or 2A to retain
5 or acquire possession of the goods in not a "security interest", but a seller or lessor may also acquire a "security
6 interest" by complying with chapter 9A. The retention or reservation of title by a seller of goods notwithstanding
7 shipment or delivery to the buyer ( 30-2-401) is limited in effect to a reservation of a "security interest". Whether
8 a transaction in the form of a lease creates a "security interest" is determined pursuant to 30-1-211.
9 (kk) "Send" in connection with a writing, record, or notice notification means:
10 (i) to deposit in the mail, or deliver for transmission, or transmit by any other usual means of
11 communication, with postage or cost of transmission provided for, and properly addressed, and in the case of
12 an instrument, to an address specified thereon or otherwise agreed, or if there be none addressed to any
13 address reasonable under the circumstances; or
14 (ii) in any other way to cause to be received any record or notice within the time it would have
15 arrived if properly sent to cause the record or notification to be received within the time it would have been
16 received if properly sent under subsection (2)(kk)(i).
17 (ll) (i) "Signed" includes any symbol executed or adopted with present intention to adopt or accept
18 a writing.“Sign” means, with present intent to authenticate or adopt a record:
19 (A) to execute or adopt a tangible symbol; or
20 (B) to attach to or logically associate with the record an electronic symbol, sound, or process.
21 (ii) “Signed”, “signing”, and “signature” have corresponding meanings.
22 (mm) "Surety" includes a guarantor or other secondary obligor.
23 (nn) "Term" means a portion of an agreement that relates to a particular matter.
24 (oo) "Unauthorized" signature means a signature made without actual, implied, or apparent
25 authority. The term includes a forgery.
26 (pp) "Warehouse receipt" means a document of title issued by a person engaged in the business of
27 storing goods for hire.
28 (qq) "Writing" includes printing, typewriting, or any other intentional reduction to tangible form.

3 Section 4. Section 30-1-212, MCA, is amended to read:
4 "30-1-212. Value. Except as otherwise provided in chapters 3 through 5 and [sections 94 through
5 109], a person gives value for rights if the person acquires them:
6 (1) in return for a binding commitment to extend credit or for the extension of immediately available
7 credit, whether or not drawn upon and whether or not a charge-back is provided for in the event of difficulties in
8 collection;
9 (2) as security for, or in total or partial satisfaction of, a preexisting claim;
10 (3) by accepting delivery under a preexisting contract for purchase; or
11 (4) in return for any consideration sufficient to support a simple contract."
12
13 Section 5. Section 30-1-301, MCA, is amended to read:
14 "30-1-301. Territorial applicability -- parties power to choose applicable law. (1) Except as
15 otherwise provided in this section, when a transaction bears a reasonable relation to this state and also to
16 another state or nation, the parties may agree that the law either of this state or of the other state or nation shall
17 govern their rights and duties.
18 (2) In the absence of an agreement effective under subsection (1) and except as provided in
19 subsection (3), this code applies to transactions bearing an appropriate relation to this state.
20 (3) If one of the following provisions of this code specifies the applicable law, that provision
21 governs and a contrary agreement is effective only to the extent permitted by the law so specified:
22 (a) Section 30-2-402;
23 (b) Sections 30-2A-105 and 30-2A-106;
24 (c) Section 30-4-102;
25 (d) Section 30-4A-507;
26 (e) Section 30-5-136;

3 Section 6. Section 30-2-102, MCA, is amended to read:
4 "30-2-102. Scope -- certain security and other transactions excluded from this chapter. (1)
5 Unless the context otherwise requires, and except as provided in subsection (3), this chapter applies to
6 transactions in goods; it does not apply to any transaction which although in the form of an unconditional
7 contract to sell or present sale is intended to operate only as a security transaction nor does this chapter impair
8 or repeal any statute regulating sales to consumers, farmers or other specified classes of buyers and, in the
9 case of a hybrid transaction, it applies to the extent provided in subsection (2).
10 (2) In a hybrid transaction:
11 (a) if the sale-of-goods aspects do not predominate, only the provisions of this chapter that relate
12 primarily to the sale-of-goods aspects of the transaction apply, and the provisions that relate primarily to the
13 transaction as a whole do not apply;
14 (b) if the sale-of-goods aspects predominate, this chapter applies to the transaction but does not
15 preclude application in appropriate circumstances of other law to aspects of the transaction that do not relate to
16 the sale of goods.
17 (3) This chapter does not:
18 (a) apply to a transaction that, even though in the form of an unconditional contract to sell or
19 present sale, operates only to create a security interest; or
20 (b) impair or repeal a statute regulating sales to consumers, farmers, or other specified classes of
21 buyers."
22
23 Section 7. Section 30-2-106, MCA, is amended to read:
24 "30-2-106. Definitions -- "contract" -- "agreement" -- "contract for sale" -- "sale" -- "present
25 sale" -- "conforming" to contract -- "termination" -- "cancellation" -- "hybrid transaction". (1) In this
26 chapter unless the context otherwise requires "contract" and "agreement" are limited to those relating to the
27 present or future sale of goods. "Contract for sale" includes both a present sale of goods and a contract to sell
28 goods at a future time. A "sale" consists in the passing of title from the seller to the buyer for a price ( 30-2-
- 9 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 401). A "present sale" means a sale which is accomplished by the making of the contract.
2 (2) Goods or conduct including any part of a performance are "conforming" or conform to the
3 contract when they are in accordance with the obligations under the contract.
4 (3) "Termination" occurs when either party pursuant to a power created by agreement or law puts
5 an end to the contract otherwise than for its breach. On "termination" all obligations which are still executory on
6 both sides are discharged but any right based on prior breach or performance survives.
7 (4) "Cancellation" occurs when either party puts an end to the contract for breach by the other and
8 its effect is the same as that of "termination" except that the canceling party also retains any remedy for breach
9 of the whole contract or any unperformed balance.
10 (5) “Hybrid transaction” means a single transaction involving a sale of goods and:
11 (a) the provision of services;
12 (b) a lease of other goods; or
13 (c) a sale, lease, or license of property other than goods."
14
15 Section 8. Section 30-2-201, MCA, is amended to read:
16 "30-2-201. Formal requirements -- statute of frauds. (1) Except as otherwise provided in this
17 section a contract for the sale of goods for the price of $500 or more is not enforceable by way of action or
18 defense unless there is some writing a record sufficient to indicate that a contract for sale has been made
19 between the parties and signed by the party against whom enforcement is sought or by the party's authorized
20 agent or broker. A writing record is not insufficient because it omits or incorrectly states a term agreed upon but
21 the contract is not enforceable under this subsection beyond the quantity of goods shown in the writing record.
22 (2) Between merchants if within a reasonable time a writing record in confirmation of the contract
23 and sufficient against the sender is received and the party receiving it has reason to know its contents, it
24 satisfies the requirements of subsection (1) against the party unless written notice in a record of objection to its
25 contents is given within 10 days after it is received.
26 (3) A contract which does not satisfy the requirements of subsection (1) but which is valid in other
27 respects is enforceable:
28 (a) if the goods are to be specially manufactured for the buyer and are not suitable for sale to
- 10 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 others in the ordinary course of the seller's business and the seller, before notice of repudiation is received and
2 under circumstances which reasonably indicate that the goods are for the buyer, has made either a substantial
3 beginning of their manufacture or commitments for their procurement; or
4 (b) if the party against whom enforcement is sought admits in the party's pleading, testimony, or
5 otherwise in court that a contract for sale was made, but the contract is not enforceable under this provision
6 beyond the quantity of goods admitted; or
7 (c) with respect to goods for which payment has been made and accepted or which have been
8 received and accepted ( 30-2-606)."
9
10 Section 9. Section 30-2-202, MCA, is amended to read:
11 "30-2-202. Final written expression -- parol or extrinsic evidence. Terms with respect to which the
12 confirmatory memoranda of the parties agree or which are otherwise set forth in a writing record intended by
13 the parties as a final expression of their agreement with respect to such terms as are included therein may not
14 be contradicted by evidence of any prior agreement or of a contemporaneous oral agreement but may be
15 explained or supplemented:
16 (a) (1) by course of dealing or usage of trade ( 30-1-205) or by course of performance ( 30-2-208);
17 and
18 (b) (2) by evidence of consistent additional terms unless the court finds the writing to have been
19 intended also as a complete and exclusive statement of the terms of the agreement."
20
21 Section 10. Section 30-2-203, MCA, is amended to read:
22 "30-2-203. Seals inoperative. The affixing of a seal to a writing record evidencing a contract for sale
23 or an offer to buy or sell goods does not constitute the writing record a sealed instrument and the law with
24 respect to sealed instruments does not apply to such a contract or offer."
25
26 Section 11. Section 30-2-205, MCA, is amended to read:
27 "30-2-205. Firm offers. An offer by a merchant to buy or sell goods in a signed writing record which
28 by its terms gives assurance that it will be held open is not revocable, for lack of consideration, during the time
- 11 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 stated or if no time is stated for a reasonable time, but in no event may such period of irrevocability exceed 3
2 months; but any such term of assurance on a form supplied by the offeree must be separately signed by the
3 offeror."
4
5 Section 12. Section 30-2-209, MCA, is amended to read:
6 "30-2-209. Modification, rescission and waiver. (1) An agreement modifying a contract within this
7 chapter needs no consideration to be binding.
8 (2) A signed agreement which excludes modification or rescission except by a signed writing or
9 other signed record cannot be otherwise modified or rescinded, but except as between merchants such a
10 requirement on a form supplied by the merchant must be separately signed by the other party.
11 (3) The requirements of the statute of frauds section of this chapter ( 30-2-201) must be satisfied if
12 the contract as modified is within its provisions.
13 (4) Although an attempt at modification or rescission does not satisfy the requirements of
14 subsection (2) or (3) it can operate as a waiver.
15 (5) A party who has made a waiver affecting an executory portion of the contract may retract the
16 waiver by reasonable notification received by the other party that strict performance will be required of any term
17 waived, unless the retraction would be unjust in view of a material change of position in reliance on the waiver."
18
19 Section 13. Section 30-2A-102, MCA, is amended to read:
20 "30-2A-102. Scope. (1) This chapter applies to any transaction, regardless of form, that creates a
21 lease and, in the case of a hybrid lease, this chapter applies to the extent provided in subsection (2).
22 (2) In a hybrid lease:
23 (a) if the lease-of-goods aspects do not predominate:
24 (i) only the provisions of this chapter that relate primarily to the lease-of-goods aspects of the
25 transaction apply, and the provisions that relate primarily to the transaction as a whole do not apply;
26 (ii) 30-2A-209 applies if the lease is a finance lease; and
27 (iii) 30-2A-407 applies to the promises of the lessee in a finance lease to the extent the promises
28 are consideration for the right to possession and use of the leased goods; and
- 12 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 (b) if the lease-of-goods aspects predominate, this chapter applies to the transaction, but does not
2 preclude application in appropriate circumstances of other law to aspects of the lease that do not relate to the
3 lease of goods."
4
5 Section 14. Section 30-2A-103, MCA, is amended to read:
6 "30-2A-103. Definitions and index of definitions. (1) In this chapter, unless the context otherwise
7 requires, the following definitions apply:
8 (a) "Buyer in ordinary course of business" means a person, who in good faith and without
9 knowledge that the sale to the buyer is in violation of the ownership rights or security interest or leasehold
10 interest of a third party in the goods, buys in ordinary course from a person in the business of selling goods of
11 that kind, but the term does not include a pawnbroker. "Buying" may be for cash or by exchange of other
12 property or on secured or unsecured credit and includes acquiring goods or documents of title under a
13 preexisting contract for sale but does not include a transfer in bulk or as security for or in total or partial
14 satisfaction of a money debt.
15 (b) "Cancellation" occurs when either party puts an end to the lease contract for default by the
16 other party.
17 (c) "Commercial unit" means such a unit of goods as by commercial usage is a single whole for
18 purposes of lease and division of which materially impairs its character or value on the market or in use. A
19 commercial unit may be a single article, as a machine; a set of articles, as a suite of furniture or a line of
20 machinery; a quantity, as a gross or carload; or any other unit treated in use or in the relevant market as a
21 single whole.
22 (d) "Conforming" goods or performance under a lease contract means goods or performance that
23 is in accordance with the obligations under the lease contract.
24 (e) "Consumer lease" means a lease that a lessor regularly engaged in the business of leasing or
25 selling makes to a lessee who is an individual and who takes under the lease primarily for a personal, family, or
26 household purpose if the total payments to be made under the lease contract, excluding payments for options
27 to renew or buy, do not exceed $25,000.
28 (f) "Fault" means wrongful act, omission, breach, or default.

1 (g) "Finance lease" means a lease with respect to which:
2 (i) the lessor does not select, manufacture, or supply the goods;

4 with the lease; and
5 (iii) one of the following occurs:
6 (A) the lessee receives a copy of the contract by which the lessor acquired the goods or the right to
7 possession and use of the goods before signing the lease contract;
8 (B) the lessee's approval of the contract by which the lessor acquired the goods or the right to
9 possession and use of the goods is a condition to effectiveness of the lease contract;
10 (C) the lessee, before signing the lease contract, receives an accurate and complete statement
11 designating the promises and warranties, and any disclaimers of warranties, limitations or modifications of
12 remedies, or liquidated damages, including those of a third party, such as the manufacturer of the goods,
13 provided to the lessor by the person supplying the goods in connection with or as part of the contract by which
14 the lessor acquired the goods or the right to possession and use of the goods; or
15 (D) if the lease is not a consumer lease, the lessor, before the lessee signs the lease contract,
16 informs the lessee in writing:

18 that person and directed the lessor to acquire the goods or the right to possession and use of the goods from
19 that person;

10 describe the goods leased and the lease term.

12 whether or not it is specific, if it reasonably identifies what is described.

14 the lease contract is not enforceable under subsection (1)(b) beyond the lease term and the quantity of goods
15 shown in the writing record.

19 collateral; or

19 order does not provide for payment to an account.

21 (e) "Sender" means the person giving the instruction to the receiving bank.

23 beneficiary, the instruction is a separate payment order with respect to each payment.

17 Section 28. Section 30-4A-201, MCA, is amended to read:
18 "30-4A-201. Security procedure. "Security procedure" means a procedure established by agreement
19 of a customer and a receiving bank for the purpose of verifying that a payment order or communication
20 amending or canceling a payment order is that of the customer or detecting error in the transmission or the
21 content of the payment order or communication. A security procedure may impose an obligation on the
22 receiving bank or the customer and may require the use of algorithms or other codes, identifying words, or
23 numbers, symbols, sounds, biometrics, encryption, callback procedures, or similar security devices.
24 Comparison of a signature on a payment order or communication with an authorized specimen signature of the
25 customer or requiring a payment order to be sent from a known e-mail address, IP address, or telephone
26 number is not by itself a security procedure."
27
28 Section 29. Section 30-4A-202, MCA, is amended to read:
- 28 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 "30-4A-202. Authorized and verified payment orders. (1) A payment order received by the
2 receiving bank is the authorized order of the person identified as sender if that person authorized the order or is
3 otherwise bound by it under the law of agency.
4 (2) If a bank and its customer have agreed that the authenticity of payment orders issued to the
5 bank in the name of the customer as sender will be verified pursuant to a security procedure, a payment order
6 received by the receiving bank is effective as the order of the customer, whether or not authorized, if the
7 security procedure is a commercially reasonable method of providing security against unauthorized payment
8 orders and the bank proves that it accepted the payment order in good faith and in compliance with the bank's
9 obligations under the security procedure and any written agreement or instruction of the customer, evidenced
10 by a record, restricting acceptance of payment orders issued in the name of the customer. The bank is not
11 required to follow an instruction that violates a written an agreement with the customer, evidenced by a record,
12 or notice of which is not received at a time and in a manner affording the bank a reasonable opportunity to act
13 on it before the payment order is accepted.
14 (3) Commercial reasonableness of a security procedure is a question of law to be determined by
15 considering the wishes of the customer expressed to the bank, the circumstances of the customer known to the
16 bank, including the size, type, and frequency of payment orders normally issued by the customer to the bank,
17 alternative security procedures offered to the customer, and security procedures in general use by customers
18 and receiving banks similarly situated. A security procedure is considered to be commercially reasonable if:
19 (a) the security procedure was chosen by the customer after the bank offered, and the customer
20 refused, a security procedure that was commercially reasonable for that customer; and
21 (b) the customer expressly agreed in writing a record to be bound by any payment order, whether
22 or not authorized, issued in the customer's name and accepted by the bank in compliance with the bank's
23 obligation under the security procedure chosen by the customer.
24 (4) The term "sender" in this chapter includes the customer in whose name a payment order is
25 issued if the order is the authorized order of the customer under subsection (1) or if it is effective as the order of
26 the customer under subsection (2).
27 (5) This section applies to amendments and cancellations of payment orders to the same extent it
28 applies to payment orders.

22 "30-4A-207. Misdescription of beneficiary. (1) Subject to subsection (2), if, in a payment order
23 received by the beneficiary's bank, the name, bank account number, or other identification of the beneficiary
24 refers to a nonexistent or unidentifiable person or account, no person has rights as a beneficiary of the order
25 and acceptance of the order cannot occur.
26 (2) If a payment order received by the beneficiary's bank identifies the beneficiary both by name
27 and by an identifying or bank account number and the name and number identify different persons, the
28 following rules apply:
- 30 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (3), if the beneficiary's bank does not know that the
2 name and number refer to different persons, it may rely on the number as the proper identification of the
3 beneficiary of the order. The beneficiary's bank need not determine whether the name and number refer to the
4 same person.
5 (b) If the beneficiary's bank pays the person identified by name or knows that the name and
6 number identify different persons, no person has rights as beneficiary except the person paid by the
7 beneficiary's bank if that person was entitled to receive payment from the originator of the funds transfer. If no
8 person has rights as beneficiary, acceptance of the order cannot occur.
9 (3) If a payment order described in subsection (2) is accepted, the originator's payment order
10 described the beneficiary inconsistently by name and number, and the beneficiary's bank pays the person
11 identified by number as permitted by subsection (2)(a), the following rules apply:
12 (a) If the originator is a bank, the originator is obliged to pay its order.
13 (b) If the originator is not a bank and proves that the person identified by number was not entitled
14 to receive payment from the originator, the originator is not obliged to pay its order unless the originator's bank
15 proves that the originator, before acceptance of the originator's order, had notice that payment of a payment
16 order issued by the originator might be made by the beneficiary's bank on the basis of an identifying or bank
17 account number even if it identifies a person different from the named beneficiary. Proof of notice may be made
18 by any admissible evidence. The originator's bank satisfies the burden of proof if it proves that the originator,
19 before the payment order was accepted, signed a writing record stating the information to which the notice
20 relates.
21 (4) In a case governed by subsection (2)(a), if the beneficiary's bank rightfully pays the person
22 identified by number and that person was not entitled to receive payment from the originator, the amount paid
23 may be recovered from that person to the extent allowed by the law governing mistake and restitution as
24 follows:
25 (a) If the originator is obliged to pay its payment order as stated in subsection (3), the originator

5 Section 33. Section 30-4A-210, MCA, is amended to read:
6 "30-4A-210. Rejection of payment order. (1) A payment order is rejected by the receiving bank by a
7 notice of rejection transmitted to the sender orally, electronically, or in writing a record. A notice of rejection
8 need not use any particular words and is sufficient if it indicates that the receiving bank is rejecting the order or
9 will not execute or pay the order. Rejection is effective when the notice is given if transmission is by a means
10 that is reasonable in the circumstances. If notice of rejection is given by a means that is not reasonable,
11 rejection is effective when the notice is received. If an agreement of the sender and receiving bank establishes
12 the means to be used to reject a payment order:
13 (a) any means complying with the agreement is reasonable; and
14 (b) any means not complying is not reasonable unless no significant delay in receipt of the notice
15 resulted from the use of the noncomplying means.
16 (2) This subsection applies if a receiving bank other than the beneficiary's bank fails to execute a
17 payment order despite the existence on the execution date of a withdrawable credit balance in an authorized
18 account of the sender sufficient to cover the order. If the sender does not receive notice of rejection of the order
19 on the execution date and the authorized account of the sender does not bear interest, the bank is obliged to
20 pay interest to the sender on the amount of the order for the number of days elapsing after the execution date
21 to the earlier of the day the order is canceled pursuant to 30-4A-211(4) or the day the sender receives notice or
22 learns that the order was not executed, counting the final day of the period as an elapsed day. If the
23 withdrawable credit balance during that period falls below the amount of the order, the amount of interest is
24 reduced accordingly.
25 (3) If a receiving bank suspends payments, all unaccepted payment orders issued to it are
26 considered rejected at the time the bank suspends payments.
27 (4) Acceptance of a payment order precludes a later rejection of the order. Rejection of a payment
28 order precludes a later acceptance of the order."

13 if the securities intermediary has expressly agreed with the other person that the property is to be treated as a
14 financial asset under this chapter.
15 (ii) As context requires, the term means either the interest itself or the means by which a person's
16 claim to it is evidenced, including a certificated or uncertificated security, a security certificate, or a security
17 entitlement.
18 (j) "Good faith," for purposes of the obligation of good faith in the performance or enforcement of
19 contracts or duties within this chapter, means honesty in fact and the observance of reasonable commercial
20 standards of fair dealing.
21 (k) "Indorsement" means a signature that alone or accompanied by other words is made on a
22 security certificate in registered form or on a separate document for the purpose of assigning, transferring, or
23 redeeming the security or granting a power to assign, transfer, or redeem it.
24 (l) "Instruction" means a notification communicated to the issuer of an uncertificated security
25 which directs that the transfer of the security be registered or that the security be redeemed.
26 (m) "Registered form," as applied to a certificated security, means a form in which:
27 (i) the security certificate specifies a person entitled to the security; and
28 (ii) a transfer of the security may be registered upon books maintained for that purpose by or on
- 42 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426

11 Section 41. Section 30-8-113, MCA, is amended to read:
12 "30-8-113. Rules for determining whether certain obligations and interests are securities or
13 financial assets. (1) A share or similar equity interest issued by a corporation, business trust, joint-stock
14 company, or similar entity is a security.
15 (2) An "investment company security" is a security. "Investment company security" means a share
16 or similar equity interest issued by an entity that is registered as an investment company under the federal
17 investment company laws, an interest in a unit investment trust that is so registered, or a face-amount
18 certificate issued by a face-amount certificate company that is so registered. Investment company security does
19 not include an insurance policy or endowment policy or annuity contract issued by an insurance company.
20 (3) An interest in a partnership or limited liability company is not a security unless it is dealt in or
21 traded on securities exchanges or in securities markets, its terms expressly provide that it is a security
22 governed by this chapter, or it is an investment company security. However, an interest in a partnership or
23 limited liability company is a financial asset if it is held in a securities account.
24 (4) A writing that is a security certificate is governed by this chapter and not by chapter 3, even
25 though it also meets the requirements of that chapter. However, a negotiable instrument governed by chapter 3
26 is a financial asset if it is held in a securities account.
27 (5) An option or similar obligation issued by a clearing corporation to its participants is not a
28 security, but is a financial asset.

****

1 (6) A commodity contract, as defined in 30-9A-102, is not a security or a financial asset.
2 (7) A document of title, as defined in 30-1-201(2)(q) (2)(p), is not a financial asset unless 30-8-
3 112(1)(i)(C) (1)(i)(i)(C) applies.
4 (8) A controllable account, controllable electronic record, or controllable payment intangible is not

7 Section 42. Section 30-8-116, MCA, is amended to read:
8 "30-8-116. Control. (1) A purchaser has "control" of a certificated security in bearer form if the
9 certificated security is delivered to the purchaser.
10 (2) A purchaser has "control" of a certificated security in registered form if the certificated security
11 is delivered to the purchaser and:
12 (a) the certificate is indorsed to the purchaser or in blank by an effective indorsement; or
13 (b) the certificate is registered in the name of the purchaser, upon original issue or registration of
14 transfer by the issuer.
15 (3) A purchaser has "control" of an uncertificated security if:
16 (a) the uncertificated security is delivered to the purchaser; or
17 (b) the issuer has agreed that it will comply with instructions originated by the purchaser without
18 further consent by the registered owner.
19 (4) A purchaser has "control" of a security entitlement if:
20 (a) the purchaser becomes the entitlement holder;
21 (b) the securities intermediary has agreed that it will comply with entitlement orders originated by
22 the purchaser without further consent by the entitlement holder; or
23 (c) another person has control of the security entitlement on behalf of the purchaser or, having
24 previously acquired control of the security entitlement, acknowledges that it has control on behalf of the
25 purchaser another person, other than the transferor to the purchaser of an interest in the security entitlement:
26 (i) has control of the security entitlement and acknowledges that it has control on behalf of the
27 purchaser; or
28 (ii) obtains control of the security entitlement after having acknowledged that it will obtain control of
- 45 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 the security entitlement on behalf of the purchaser.
2 (5) If an interest in a security entitlement is granted by the entitlement holder to the entitlement
3 holder's own securities intermediary, the securities intermediary has control.
4 (6) A purchaser who has satisfied the requirements of subsection (3) or (4) has control even if the
5 registered owner in the case of subsection (3) or the entitlement holder in the case of subsection (4) retains the
6 right to make substitutions for the uncertificated security or security entitlement, to originate instructions or
7 entitlement orders to the issuer or securities intermediary, or otherwise to deal with the uncertificated security or
8 security entitlement.
9 (7) An issuer or a securities intermediary may not enter into an agreement of the kind described in
10 subsection (3)(b) or (4)(b) without the consent of the registered owner or entitlement holder, but an issuer or a
11 securities intermediary is not required to enter into such an agreement even though the registered owner or
12 entitlement holder so directs. An issuer or securities intermediary that has entered into such an agreement is
13 not required to confirm the existence of the agreement to another party unless requested to do so by the
14 registered owner or entitlement holder.
15 (8) A person that has control under this section is not required to acknowledge that it has control
16 on behalf of a purchaser.
17 (9) If a person acknowledges that it has or will obtain control on behalf of a purchaser, unless the
18 person otherwise agrees or law other than chapter 9A or this chapter otherwise provides, the person does not
19 owe any duty to the purchaser and is not required to confirm the acknowledgment to any other person."

3 Section 46. Section 30-9A-104, MCA, is amended to read:
4 "30-9A-104. Control of deposit account. (1) A secured party has control of a deposit account if:
5 (a) the secured party is the bank with which the deposit account is maintained;
6 (b) the debtor, secured party, and bank have agreed in an authenticated a signed record that the
7 bank will comply with instructions originated by the secured party directing disposition of the funds in the
8 deposit account without further consent by the debtor; or
9 (c) the secured party becomes the bank's customer with respect to the deposit account; or
10 (d) another person, other than the debtor:
11 (i) has control of the deposit account and acknowledges that it has control on behalf of the
12 secured party; or
13 (ii) obtains control of the deposit account after having acknowledged that it will obtain control of
14 the deposit account on behalf of the secured party.
15 (2) A secured party that has satisfied the requirements of subsection (1) has control, even if the
16 debtor retains the right to direct the disposition of funds from the deposit account."

4 NEW SECTION. Section 49. No requirement to acknowledge or confirm -- no duties. (1) A
5 person that has control under 30-9A-104 or 30-9A-105 is not required to acknowledge that it has control on
6 behalf of another person.

8 the person otherwise agrees or law other than this chapter otherwise provides, the person does not owe any
9 duty to the other person and is not required to confirm the acknowledgment to any other person.

8 (d) the secured party may use or operate the collateral:
9 (i) for the purpose of preserving the collateral or its value;
10 (ii) as permitted by an order of a court having competent jurisdiction; or
11 (iii) except in the case of consumer goods, in the manner and to the extent agreed by the debtor.
12 (3) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (4), a secured party having possession of collateral
13 or control of collateral under 30-7-107, 30-9A-104, 30-9A-105, 30-9A-106, or 30-9A-107, or [section 48]:
14 (a) may hold as additional security any proceeds, except money or funds, received from the
15 collateral;
16 (b) shall apply money or funds received from the collateral to reduce the secured obligation, unless
17 remitted to the debtor; and
18 (c) may create a security interest in the collateral.
19 (4) If the secured party is a buyer of accounts, chattel paper, payment intangibles, or promissory
20 notes or a consignor:
21 (a) subsection (1) does not apply unless the secured party is entitled by agreement:
22 (i) to charge back uncollected collateral; or
23 (ii) otherwise to full or limited recourse against the debtor or a secondary obligor based on the
24 nonpayment or other default of an account debtor or other obligor on the collateral; and
25 (b) subsections (2) and (3) do not apply."

19 NEW SECTION. Section 59. Laws governing perfection and priority of security interests in
20 chattel paper. (1) Except as provided in subsection (4), if chattel paper is evidenced only by an authoritative
21 electronic copy of the chattel paper or is evidenced by an authoritative electronic copy and an authoritative
22 tangible copy, the local law of the chattel paper’s jurisdiction governs perfection, the effect of perfection or
23 nonperfection, and the priority of a security interest in the chattel paper, even if the transaction does not bear
24 any relation to the chattel paper’s jurisdiction.
25 (2) The following rules determine the chattel paper’s jurisdiction under this section:
26 (a) If the authoritative electronic copy of the record evidencing chattel paper, or a record attached
27 to or logically associated with the electronic copy and readily available for review, expressly provides that a
28 particular jurisdiction is the chattel paper’s jurisdiction for purposes of this part, this chapter, or this code, that
- 78 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 jurisdiction is the chattel paper’s jurisdiction.
2 (b) If subsection (2)(a) does not apply and the rules of the system in which the authoritative
3 electronic copy is recorded are readily available for review and expressly provide that a particular jurisdiction is
4 the chattel paper’s jurisdiction for purposes of this part, this chapter, or this code, that jurisdiction is the chattel
5 paper’s jurisdiction.
6 (c) If subsections (2)(a) and (2)(b) do not apply and the authoritative electronic copy, or a record
7 attached to or logically associated with the electronic copy and readily available for review, expressly provides
8 that the chattel paper is governed by the law of a particular jurisdiction, that jurisdiction is the chattel paper’s
9 jurisdiction.
10 (d) If subsections (2)(a), (2)(b), and (2)(c) do not apply and the rules of the system in which the
11 authoritative electronic copy is recorded are readily available for review and expressly provide that the chattel
12 paper or the system is governed by the law of a particular jurisdiction, that jurisdiction is the chattel paper’s
13 jurisdiction.
14 (e) If subsections (2)(a) through (2)(d) do not apply, the chattel paper’s jurisdiction is the
15 jurisdiction in which the debtor is located.
16 (3) If an authoritative tangible copy of a record evidences chattel paper and the chattel paper is not
17 evidenced by an authoritative electronic copy, while the authoritative tangible copy of the record evidencing
18 chattel paper is located in a jurisdiction, the local law of that jurisdiction governs:
19 (a) perfection of a security interest in the chattel paper by possession under 30-9A-313; and
20 (b) the effect of perfection or nonperfection and the priority of a security interest in the chattel
21 paper.
22 (4) The local law of the jurisdiction in which the debtor is located governs perfection of a security
23 interest in chattel paper by filing.

13 (a) the time perfection would have ceased under the law of that jurisdiction;
14 (b) the expiration of 4 months after a change of the debtor's location to another jurisdiction;
15 (c) the expiration of 1 year after a transfer of collateral to a person that thereby becomes a debtor
16 and is located in another jurisdiction; or
17 (d) the expiration of 1 year after a new debtor located in another jurisdiction becomes bound under
18 30-9A-203(4).
19 (2) If a security interest described in subsection (1) becomes perfected under the law of the other
20 jurisdiction before the earliest time or event described in that subsection, it remains perfected thereafter. If the
21 security interest does not become perfected under the law of the other jurisdiction before the earliest time or
22 event, it becomes unperfected and is deemed never to have been perfected as against a purchaser of the
23 collateral for value.
24 (3) A possessory security interest in collateral, other than goods covered by a certificate of title and

28 (b) thereafter the collateral is brought into another jurisdiction; and

5 covered by a certificate of title from this state remains perfected until the security interest would have become

11 NEW SECTION. Section 70. Priority of security interest in controllable account, controllable
12 electronic record, and controllable payment intangible. A security interest in a controllable account,

27 NEW SECTION. Section 94. Title. [Sections 94 through 100] may be cited as the "Uniform
28 Commercial Code--Controllable Electronic Records".
- 121 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1
2 NEW SECTION. Section 95. Definitions. (1) As used in [sections 94 through 100], the following
3 definitions apply:
4 (a) (i) “Controllable electronic record” means a record stored in an electronic medium that can be
5 subjected to control under [section 98].
6 (ii) The term does not include a controllable account, a controllable payment intangible, a deposit
7 account, an electronic copy of a record evidencing chattel paper, an electronic document of title, investment
8 property, a transferable record, or an electronic record that is currently authorized or adopted by a domestic or
9 foreign government and is not a medium of exchange that was recorded and transferable in a system that
10 existed and operated for the medium of exchange before the medium of exchange was authorized or adopted
11 by a government.
12 (b) “Qualifying purchaser” means a purchaser of a controllable electronic record or an interest in a
13 controllable electronic record that obtains control of the controllable electronic record for value, in good faith,
14 and without notice of a claim of a property right in the controllable electronic record.
15 (c) “Transferable record” has the meaning provided for that term in:
16 (i) Section 201(a)(1) of the Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act, 15 U.S.C.
17 Section 7021(a)(1); or
18 (ii) 30-18-115(1).
19 (d) “Value” has the meaning provided in 30-3-303(1), as if references in that subsection to an
20 “instrument” were references to a controllable account, controllable electronic record, or controllable payment
21 intangible.
22 (2) The definitions in Title 30, chapter 9A, of “account debtor”, “controllable account”, “controllable
23 payment intangible”, “chattel paper”, “deposit account”, and “investment property” apply to [sections 94 through
24 100].
25 (3) Title 30, chapter 1, contains general definitions and principles of construction and interpretation
26 applicable throughout [sections 94 through 100].
27
28 NEW SECTION. Section 96. Relation to Title 30, chapter 9A, and consumer laws. (1) If there is
- 122 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 conflict between Title 30, chapter 9A, and [sections 94 through 100], Title 30, chapter 9A, governs.
2 (2) A transaction subject to [sections 94 through 100] is subject to any applicable rule of law that
3 establishes a different rule for consumers, Title 30, chapter 14, part 1, Title 31, chapter 1, and Title 32, chapter
4 6, part 1.
5
6 NEW SECTION. Section 97. Rights in controllable account, controllable electronic record, and
7 controllable payment intangible. (1) This section applies to the acquisition and purchase of rights in a
8 controllable account or controllable payment intangible, including the rights and benefits under subsections (3),
9 (4), (5), (7), and (8) of a purchaser and qualifying purchaser, in the same manner this section applies to a
10 controllable electronic record.
11 (2) To determine whether a purchaser of a controllable account or a controllable payment
12 intangible is a qualifying purchaser, the purchaser obtains control of the account or payment intangible if it
13 obtains control of the controllable electronic record that evidences the account or payment intangible.
14 (3) Except as provided in this section, law other than [sections 94 through 100] determines
15 whether a person acquires a right in a controllable electronic record and the right the person acquires.
16 (4) A purchaser of a controllable electronic record acquires all rights in the controllable electronic
17 record that the transferor had or had power to transfer, except that a purchaser of a limited interest in a
18 controllable electronic record acquires rights only to the extent of the interest purchased.
19 (5) A qualifying purchaser acquires its rights in the controllable electronic record free of a claim of
20 a property right in the controllable electronic record.
21 (6) Except as provided in subsections (1) and (5) for a controllable account and a controllable
22 payment intangible or law other than [sections 94 through 100], a qualifying purchaser takes a right to payment,
23 right to performance, or other interest in property evidenced by the controllable electronic record subject to a
24 claim of a property right in the right to payment, right to performance, or other interest in property.
25 (7) An action may not be asserted against a qualifying purchaser based on both a purchase by the
26 qualifying purchaser of a controllable electronic record and a claim of a property right in another controllable
27 electronic record, whether the action is framed in conversion, replevin, constructive trust, equitable lien, or other
28 theory.
- 123 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 (8) Filing of a financing statement under Title 30, chapter 9A, is not notice of a claim of a property
2 right in a controllable electronic record.
3
4 NEW SECTION. Section 98. Control of controllable electronic record. (1) A person has control of
5 a controllable electronic record if the electronic record, a record attached to or logically associated with the
6 electronic record, or a system in which the electronic record is recorded:
7 (a) gives the person:
8 (i) power to avail itself of substantially all the benefit from the electronic record; and
9 (ii) exclusive power, subject to subsection (2), to:
10 (A) prevent others from availing themselves of substantially all the benefit from the electronic
11 record; and
12 (B) transfer control of the electronic record to another person or cause another person to obtain
13 control of another controllable electronic record as a result of the transfer of the electronic record; and
14 (b) enables the person readily to identify itself in any way, including by name, identifying number,
15 cryptographic key, office, or account number, as having the powers specified in subjection (1)(a).
16 (2) Subject to subsection (3), a power is exclusive under subsection (1)(a)(ii)(A) and (1)(a)(ii)(B)
17 even if:
18 (a) the controllable electronic record, a record attached to or logically associated with the
19 electronic record, or a system in which the electronic record is recorded limits the use of the electronic record or
20 has a protocol programmed to cause a change, including a transfer or loss of control or a modification of
21 benefits afforded by the electronic record; or
22 (b) the power is shared with another person.
23 (3) A power of a person is not shared with another person under subsection (2)(b) and the
24 person’s power is not exclusive if:
25 (a) the person can exercise the power only if the power also is exercised by the other person; and
26 (b) the other person:
27 (i) can exercise the power without exercise of the power by the person; or
28 (ii) is the transferor to the person of an interest in the controllable electronic record or a
- 124 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 controllable account or controllable payment intangible evidenced by the controllable electronic record.
2 (4) If a person has the powers specified in subsections (1)(a)(ii)(A) and (1)(a)(ii)(B), the powers are
3 presumed to be exclusive.
4 (5) A person has control of a controllable electronic record if another person, other than the
5 transferor to the person of an interest in the controllable electronic record or a controllable account or
6 controllable payment intangible evidenced by the controllable electronic record:
7 (a) has control of the electronic record and acknowledges that it has control on behalf of the
8 person; or
9 (b) obtains control of the electronic record after having acknowledged that it will obtain control of
10 the electronic record on behalf of the person.
11 (6) A person that has control under this section is not required to acknowledge that it has control
12 on behalf of another person.
13 (7) If a person acknowledges that it has or will obtain control on behalf of another person, unless
14 the person otherwise agrees or a law other than Title 30, chapter 9A, or [sections 94 through 100] otherwise
15 provides, the person does not owe any duty to the other person and is not required to confirm the
16 acknowledgment to any other person.
17
18 NEW SECTION. Section 99. Discharge of account debtor on controllable account or
19 controllable payment intangible. (1) An account debtor on a controllable account or controllable payment
20 intangible may discharge its obligation by paying:
21 (a) the person having control of the controllable electronic record that evidences the controllable
22 account or controllable payment intangible; or
23 (b) except as provided in subsection (2), a person that formerly had control of the controllable
24 electronic record.
25 (2) Subject to subsection (4), the account debtor may not discharge its obligation by paying a
26 person that formerly had control of the controllable electronic record if the account debtor receives a notification
27 that:
28 (a) is signed by a person that formerly had control or the person to which control was transferred;
- 125 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 (b) reasonably identifies the controllable account or controllable payment intangible;
2 (c) notifies the account debtor that control of the controllable electronic record that evidences the
3 controllable account or controllable payment intangible was transferred;
4 (d) identifies the transferee, in any reasonable way, including by name, identifying number,
5 cryptographic key, office, or account number; and
6 (e) provides a commercially reasonable method by which the account debtor is to pay the
7 transferee.
8 (3) After receipt of a notification that complies with subsection (2), the account debtor may
9 discharge its obligation by paying in accordance with the notification and may not discharge the obligation by
10 paying a person that formerly had control.
11 (4) Subject to subsection (8), notification is ineffective under subsection (2):
12 (a) unless, before the notification is sent, the account debtor and the person that, at that time, had
13 control of the controllable electronic record that evidences the controllable account or controllable payment
14 intangible agree in a signed record to a commercially reasonable method by which a person may furnish
15 reasonable proof that control has been transferred;
16 (b) to the extent an agreement between the account debtor and seller of a payment intangible
17 limits the account debtor’s duty to pay a person other than the seller and the limitation is effective under law
18 other than [sections 94 through 100]; or
19 (c) at the option of the account debtor, if the notification notifies the account debtor to:
20 (i) divide a payment;
21 (ii) make less than the full amount of an installment or other periodic payment; or
22 (iii) pay any part of a payment by more than one method or to more than one person.
23 (5) Subject to subsection (8), if requested by the account debtor, the person giving the notification
24 under subsection (2) seasonably shall furnish reasonable proof, using the method in the agreement referred to
25 in subsection (4)(a), that control of the controllable electronic record has been transferred. Unless the person
26 complies with the request, the account debtor may discharge its obligation by paying a person that formerly had
27 control, even if the account debtor has received a notification under subsection (2).
28 (6) A person furnishes reasonable proof under subsection (5) that control has been transferred if
- 126 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 the person demonstrates, using the method in the agreement referred to in subsection (4)(a), that the
2 transferee has the power to:
3 (a) avail itself of substantially all the benefit from the controllable electronic record;
4 (b) prevent others from availing themselves of substantially all the benefit from the controllable
5 electronic record; and
6 (c) transfer the powers specified in subsections (6)(a) and (6)(b) to another person.
7 (7) Subject to subsection (8), an account debtor may not waive or vary its rights under subsections
8 (4)(a) and (5) or its option under subsection (4)(c).
9 (8) This section is subject to law other than [sections 94 through 100] which establishes a different
10 rule for an account debtor who is an individual and who incurred the obligation primarily for personal, family, or
11 household purposes.
12
13 NEW SECTION. Section 100. Governing law. (1) (1) Except as provided in subsection (2), the local
14 law of a controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction governs a matter covered by [sections 94 through 100].
15 (2) For a controllable electronic record that evidences a controllable account or controllable
16 payment intangible, the local law of the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction governs a matter covered by
17 [section 99] unless an effective agreement determines that the local law of another jurisdiction governs.
18 (3) The following rules determine a controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction under this section:
19 (a) If the controllable electronic record, or a record attached to or logically associated with the
20 controllable electronic record and readily available for review, expressly provides that a particular jurisdiction is
21 the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction for purposes of this code or [sections 94 through 100], that
22 jurisdiction is the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction.
23 (b) If subsection (3)(a) does not apply and the rules of the system in which the controllable
24 electronic record is recorded are readily available for review and expressly provide that a particular jurisdiction
25 is the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction for purposes of this code or [sections 94 through 100], that
26 jurisdiction is the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction.
27 (c) If subsections (3)(a) and (3)(b) do not apply and the controllable electronic record, or a record
28 attached to or logically associated with the controllable electronic record and readily available for review,
- 127 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 expressly provides that the controllable electronic record is governed by the law of a particular jurisdiction, that
2 jurisdiction is the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction.
3 (d) If subsections (3)(a) through (3)(c) do not apply and the rules of the system in which the
4 controllable electronic record is recorded are readily available for review and expressly provide that the
5 controllable electronic record or the system is governed by the law of a particular jurisdiction, that jurisdiction is
6 the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction.
7 (e) If subsections (3)(a) through (3)(d) do not apply, the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction
8 is the District of Columbia.
9 (4) (a) If subsection (3)(e) applies and [sections 94 through 100] are not in effect in the District of
10 Columbia without material modification, the governing law for a matter covered by [sections 94 through 100] is
11 the law of the District of Columbia as though [sections 94 through 100] were in effect in the District of Columbia
12 without material modification.
13 (b) In this subsection (4), “[sections 94 through 100]" means Article 12 of Uniform Commercial
14 Code Amendments (2022).
15 (5) To the extent subsections (1) and (2) provide that the local law of the controllable electronic
16 record’s jurisdiction governs a matter covered by [sections 94 through 100], that law governs even if the matter
17 or a transaction to which the matter relates does not bear any relation to the controllable electronic record’s
18 jurisdiction.
19 (6) The rights acquired under [section 95] by a purchaser or qualifying purchaser are governed by
20 the law applicable under this section at the time of purchase.
21
22 NEW SECTION. Section 101. Title. [Sections 101 through 109] may be cited as the "Transitional
23 Provisions for Uniform Commercial Code Amendments (2022)".
24
25 NEW SECTION. Section 102. Definitions. (1) In [sections 101 through 109], the following definitions
26 apply:
27 (a) “Adjustment date” means July 1, 2025, or the date that is 1 year after [the effective date of this
28 act], whichever is later.
- 128 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 (b) “[Sections 94 through 100]” means Chapter 12 of the Uniform Commercial Code.
2 (c) “Chapter 12 property” means a controllable account, controllable electronic record, or
3 controllable payment intangible.
4 (2) The following definitions in other articles of the Uniform Commercial Code apply to [sections
5 101 through 109]:
6 (a) “Controllable account”. 30-9A-102.
7 (b) “Controllable electronic record”. [Section 95].
8 (c) “Controllable payment intangible”. 30-9A-102.
9 (d) “Financing statement”. 30-9A-102.
10 (3) Title 30, chapter 1, contains general definitions and principles of construction and interpretation
11 applicable throughout [sections 101 through 109].
12
13 NEW SECTION. Section 103. Savings clause. Except as provided in [sections 102 through 107], a
14 transaction validly entered into before [the effective date of this act] and the rights, duties, and interests flowing
15 from the transaction remain valid thereafter and may be terminated, completed, consummated, or enforced as
16 required or permitted by law other than the Uniform Commercial Code or, if applicable, the Uniform Commercial
17 Code, as though [this act] had not taken effect.
18
19 NEW SECTION. Section 104. Savings clause. (1) Except as provided in [sections 102 through 107],
20 Title 30, chapter 9A, as amended by [this act] and [sections 94 through 100] apply to a transaction, lien, or
21 other interest in property, even if the transaction, lien, or interest was entered into, created, or acquired before
22 [the effective date of this act].
23 (2) Except as provided in subsection (3) and [sections 103 through 107]:
24 (a) a transaction, lien, or interest in property that was validly entered into, created, or transferred
25 before [the effective date of this act] and was not governed by the Uniform Commercial Code, but would be
26 subject to Title 30, chapter 9A, as amended by [this act] or [sections 94 through 100] if it had been entered into,
27 created, or transferred on or after [the effective date of this act], including the rights, duties, and interests
28 flowing from the transaction, lien, or interest, remains valid on and after [the effective date of this act]; and
- 129 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 (b) the transaction, lien, or interest may be terminated, completed, consummated, and enforced as
2 required or permitted by [this act] or by the law that would apply if [this act] had not taken effect.
3 (3) [This act] does not affect an action, case, or proceeding commenced before [the effective date
4 of this act].
5
6 NEW SECTION. Section 105. Security interest perfected before effective date. (1) A security
7 interest that is enforceable and perfected immediately before [the effective date of this act] is a perfected
8 security interest under [this act] if, on [the effective date of this act], the requirements for enforceability and
9 perfection under [this act] are satisfied without further action.
10 (2) If a security interest is enforceable and perfected immediately before [the effective date of this
11 act], but the requirements for enforceability or perfection under [this act] are not satisfied on [the effective date
12 of this act], the security interest:
13 (a) is a perfected security interest until the earlier of the time perfection would have ceased under
14 the law in effect immediately before [the effective date of this act] or the adjustment date;
15 (b) remains enforceable thereafter only if the security interest satisfies the requirements for
16 enforceability under 30-9A-203, as amended by [this act], before the adjustment date; and
17 (c) remains perfected thereafter only if the requirements for perfection under [this act] are satisfied
18 before the time specified in subsection (2)(a).
19
20 NEW SECTION. Section 106. Security interest unperfected before effective date. A security
21 interest that is enforceable immediately before [the effective date of this act] but is unperfected at that time:
22 (1) remains an enforceable security interest until the adjustment date;
23 (2) remains enforceable thereafter if the security interest becomes enforceable under 30-9A-203,
24 as amended by [this act], on [the effective date of this act] or before the adjustment date; and
25 (3) becomes perfected:
26 (a) without further action, on [the effective date of this act] if the requirements for perfection under
27 [this act] are satisfied before or at that time; or
28 (b) when the requirements for perfection are satisfied if the requirements are satisfied after that
- 130 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 time.
2
3 NEW SECTION. Section 107. Effectiveness of actions taken before effective date. (1) If action,
4 other than the filing of a financing statement, is taken before [the effective date of this act] and the action would
5 have resulted in perfection of the security interest had the security interest become enforceable before [the
6 effective date of this act], the action is effective to perfect a security interest that attaches under [this act] before
7 the adjustment date. An attached security interest becomes unperfected on the adjustment date unless the
8 security interest becomes a perfected security interest under [this act] before the adjustment date.
9 (2) The filing of a financing statement before [the effective date of this act] is effective to perfect a
10 security interest on [the effective date of this act] to the extent the filing would satisfy the requirements for
11 perfection under [this act].
12 (3) The taking of an action before [the effective date of this act] is sufficient for the enforceability of
13 a security interest on [the effective date of this act] if the action would satisfy the requirements for enforceability
14 under [this act].
15
16 NEW SECTION. Section 108. Priority. (1) Subject to subsections (2) and (3), [this act] determines
17 the priority of conflicting claims to collateral.
18 (2) Subject to subsection (3), if the priorities of claims to collateral were established before [the
19 effective date of this act], Title 30, chapter 9A, as in effect before [the effective date of this act] determines
20 priority.
21 (3) On the adjustment date, to the extent the priorities determined by Title 30, chapter 9A, as
22 amended by [this act], modify the priorities established before [the effective date of this act], the priorities of
23 claims to [sections 94 through 100] property established before [the effective date of this act] cease to apply.
24
25 NEW SECTION. Section 109. Priority of claims when priority rules of Title 30, chapter 9A, do
26 not apply. (1) Subject to subsections (2) and (3), [sections 94 through 100] determine the priority of conflicting
27 claims to [sections 94 through 100] property when the priority rules of Title 30, chapter 9A, as amended by [this
28 act] do not apply.
- 131 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 (2) Subject to subsection (3), when the priority rules of Title 30, chapter 9A, as amended by [this
2 act] do not apply and the priorities of claims to [sections 94 through 100] property were established before [the
3 effective date of this act], law other than [sections 94 through 100] determines priority.
4 (3) When the priority rules of Title 30, chapter 9A, as amended by [this act] do not apply, to the
5 extent the priorities determined by [this act] modify the priorities established before [the effective date of this
6 act], the priorities of claims to [sections 94 through 100] property established before [the effective date of this
7 act] cease to apply on the adjustment date.
