9 Section 110. Section 71-3-125, MCA, is amended to read:
10 "71-3-125. Filing of agricultural lien statements. (1) Unless a statement of an agricultural lien has
11 been filed in the office of the secretary of state as provided in this chapter, a buyer who, in ordinary course of
12 business as defined in 30-1-201(2)(j) (2)(i), buys a farm product takes it free of any lien created by this chapter
13 even though the lien is otherwise perfected.
14 (2) A statement of an agricultural lien is sufficient if it:
15 (a) gives the names and addresses of the debtor and lienor;
16 (b) describes the type of lien and its statutory authority;
17 (c) describes the collateral;
18 (d) contains the notation by the secretary of state of the date of filing and filing number;
19 (e) is signed by the lienor;
20 (f) describes the service or product furnished. If the collateral is farm products, the statement must
21 state the county in which the farm products are located, designated by type of farm product.
22 (g) states the price or wage agreed upon or, if the price or wage was not agreed upon, the
23 reasonable value of the service or product furnished;
24 (h) states the amount remaining unpaid;
25 (i) states the terms and period of employment if it is a farm laborer's lien filed pursuant to part 4 of
26 this chapter;
27 (j) describes the land upon which seed or grain was or will be sown, planted, or used if it is a lien
28 for seed or grain filed pursuant to part 7 of this chapter;
- 132 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426
****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 (k) describes the land upon which the grain or crops were grown and the place the grain or crops
2 are presently stored if it is a thresher's lien filed pursuant to part 8 of this chapter;
3 (l) describes the land upon which the service was performed if it is a lien for spraying or dusting
4 filed pursuant to part 9 of this chapter; and
5 (m) states the starting date of insurance coverage if it is a lien filed pursuant to part 7 of this
6 chapter.
7 (3) The agricultural lien statement must be in the form prescribed by the secretary of state.
8 (4) The secretary of state shall:
9 (a) record the agricultural lien statement on the centralized computer system as set forth in 30-9A-
10 501; and
11 (b) establish fees for such recordings as set forth in 30-9A-525.
12 (5) For the purposes of this section, an agricultural lien means a lien under part 4, 7, 8, or 9 of this
13 chapter.
14 (6) A statement of an agricultural lien or continuation statement that has been filed at the office of
15 the county clerk and recorder lapses on March 31, 1990, unless prior to that date there is filed in the office of
16 the secretary of state a certified copy of the statement and all related documents on file with the county clerk
17 and recorder."

19 NEW SECTION. Section 111. Central bank digital currency -- approval by state. As applicable in
20 this state, the term "money" does not include any central bank digital currency or any requirement to accept or
21 use a central bank digital currency, unless the central bank digital currency is specifically recognized and
22 approved by Montana law.

26 (2) [Section 49] is intended to be codified as 30-9A-107B, and the provisions of Title 30, chapters 1
27 through 9A, apply to [section 49].

1 through 9A, apply to [section 59].

20 NEW SECTION. Section 114. Severability. If a part of [this act] is invalid, all valid parts that are
21 severable from the invalid part remain in effect. If a part of [this act] is invalid in one or more of its applications,
22 the part remains in effect in all valid applications that are severable from the invalid applications.

69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 SENATE BILL NO. 426
2 INTRODUCED BY V. RICCI
3
4 A BILL FOR AN ACT ENTITLED: “AN ACT GENERALLY REVISING THE UNIFORM COMMERCIAL CODE;
5 UPDATING TERMINOLOGY FOR THE DIGITAL AGE; PROVIDING RULES FOR TRANSACTIONS
6 INVOLVING CERTAIN DIGITAL ASSETS INCLUDING CRYPTOCURRENCY; PROHIBITING CENTRAL
7 BANK DIGITAL CURRENCY; AND AMENDING SECTIONS 30-1-101, 30-1-107, 30-1-201, 30-1-212, 30-1-301,
8 30-2-102, 30-2-106, 30-2-201, 30-2-202, 30-2-203, 30-2-205, 30-2-209, 30-2A-102, 30-2A-103, 30-2A-107, 30-
9 2A-201, 30-2A-202, 30-2A-203, 30-2A-205, 30-2A-208, 30-3-102, 30-3-104, 30-3-125, 30-3-401, 30-3-605, 30-
10 4A-103, 30-4A-105, 30-4A-201, 30-4A-202, 30-4A-203, 30-4A-207, 30-4A-208, 30-4A-210, 30-4A-211, 30-4A-
11 305, 30-5-124, 30-5-136, 30-7-102, 30-7-107, 30-8-112, 30-8-113, 30-8-116, 30-8-120, 30-8-333, 30-9A-102,
12 30-9A-104, 30-9A-105, 30-9A-203, 30-9A-204, 30-9A-207, 30-9A-208, 30-9A-209, 30-9A-210, 30-9A-301, 30-
13 9A-304, 30-9A-305, 30-9A-310, 30-9A-312, 30-9A-313, 30-9A-314, 30-9A-316, 30-9A-317, 30-9A-323, 30-9A-
14 324, 30-9A-330, 30-9A-331, 30-9A-332, 30-9A-334, 30-9A-341, 30-9A-404, 30-9A-406, 30-9A-408, 30-9A-509,
15 30-9A-513, 30-9A-601, 30-9A-605, 30-9A-608, 30-9A-611, 30-9A-613, 30-9A-614, 30-9A-615, 30-9A-616, 30-
16 9A-619, 30-9A-620, 30-9A-621, 30-9A-624, 30-9A-628, AND 71-3-125, MCA.”
17
18 WHEREAS, a central bank digital currency has been defined by the Federal Reserve as a digital form
19 of central bank money that is widely available to the general public; and
20 WHEREAS, central bank money refers to money that is a liability of the central bank and not of a
21 commercial bank; and
22 WHEREAS, countries around the world, including the United States, are evaluating whether or not to
23 issue and how to issue and operate a central bank digital currency; and
24 WHEREAS, a central bank digital currency would fundamentally reimagine our banking and financial
25 system by changing the relationship between citizens and the Federal Reserve; and
26 WHEREAS, a central bank digital currency would severely undermine financial privacy for citizens; and
27 WHEREAS, the availability of a central bank digital currency in the United States would undermine the
28 important role banks play in financial intermediation and limit credit availability because funds would move from
- 1 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426

****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 commercial banks to the Federal Reserve where they cannot be lent back into the economy; and
2 WHEREAS, a central bank digital currency would fundamentally rewire our banking and financial
3 system by changing the relationship between citizens and the Federal Reserve.
4
5 BE IT ENACTED BY THE LEGISLATURE OF THE STATE OF MONTANA:
6
7 Section 1. Section 30-1-101, MCA, is amended to read:
8 "30-1-101. Short titles -- scope of chapter. (1) Chapters 1 through 9A and [sections 94 through 109]
9 of this title may be cited as Uniform Commercial Code.
10 (2) As used in chapters 1 through 9A and [sections 94 through 109] of this title "code" means
11 "Uniform Commercial Code" unless the context indicates otherwise.
12 (3) This chapter may be cited as the Uniform Commercial Code--General Provisions.
13 (4) This chapter applies to a transaction to the extent that it is governed by chapters 2 through 5,
14 7, 8, and 9A, and [sections 94 through 109] of this title.
15 (5) Nothing in chapters 1 through 9A and [sections 94 through 109] of this title may be construed to
16 support, endorse, create, or implement a national digital currency."
17
18 Section 2. Section 30-1-107, MCA, is amended to read:
19 "30-1-107. Waiver or renunciation of claim or right after breach. A claim or right arising out of an
20 alleged breach may be discharged in whole or in part without consideration by agreement of the aggrieved
21 party in an authenticated a signed record."
22
23 Section 3. Section 30-1-201, MCA, is amended to read:
24 "30-1-201. General definitions. (1) Unless the context requires otherwise, words or phrases defined
25 in this section, or in the additional definitions contained in other chapters of the code that apply to particular
26 chapters or parts of chapters, have the meanings stated.
27 (2) Subject to additional definitions contained in other chapters of this code that apply to specific
28 chapters or parts of chapters:
- 2 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426

****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 (a) "Action" in the sense of a judicial proceeding includes recoupment, counterclaim, setoff, suit in
2 equity, and any other proceeding in which rights are determined.
3 (b) "Aggrieved party" means a party entitled to pursue a remedy.
4 (c) "Agreement" means the bargain of the parties in fact, as found in their language or inferred
5 from other circumstances, including course of performance, course of dealing, or usage of trade as provided in
6 30-1-205.
7 (d) "Authenticate" means to:
8 (i) sign; or
9 (ii) execute or adopt a symbol, or encrypt a record in whole or in part, with present intent to:
10 (A) identify the authenticating party; and
11 (B) adopt, accept, or establish the authenticity of a record or term.
12 (e) (d) "Bank" means any person engaged in the business of banking and includes a savings bank,
13 savings and loan association, credit union, and trust company.
14 (f) (e) "Bearer" means a person in control of a negotiable electronic document of title or a person in
15 possession of a negotiable instrument, negotiable tangible document of title, or certificated security payable to
16 bearer or endorsed in blank.
17 (g) (f) (i) "Bill of lading" means a document of title evidencing the receipt of goods for shipment issued
18 by a person engaged in the business of directly or indirectly transporting or forwarding goods.
19 (ii) The term does not include a warehouse receipt.
20 (h) (g) "Branch" includes a separately incorporated foreign branch of a bank.
21 (i) (h) "Burden of establishing" a fact means the burden of persuading the trier of fact that the
22 existence of the fact is more probable than its nonexistence.
23 (j) (i) "Buyer in ordinary course of business" means a person that buys goods, in good faith, without
24 knowledge that the sale violates the rights of another person in the goods, and in the ordinary course from a
25 person, other than a pawnbroker, in the business of selling goods of that kind. A person buys goods in the
26 ordinary course if the sale to the person comports with the usual or customary practices in the kind of business
27 in which the seller is engaged or with the seller's own usual or customary practices. A person that sells oil, gas,
28 or other minerals at the wellhead or minehead is a person in the business of selling goods of that kind. A buyer
- 3 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426

****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 in ordinary course of business may buy for cash, by exchange of other property, or on secured or unsecured
2 credit, and may acquire goods or documents of title under a preexisting contract for sale. Only a buyer that
3 takes possession of the goods or has a right to recover the goods from the seller under chapter 2 may be a
4 buyer in ordinary course of business. A person that acquires goods in a transfer in bulk or as security for or in
5 total or partial satisfaction of a money debt is not a buyer in ordinary course of business.
6 (k) (j) "Conspicuous", with reference to a term, means so written, displayed, or presented that, based
7 on the totality of the circumstances, a reasonable person against which it is to operate ought to have noticed it.
8 Whether a term is "conspicuous" or not is for decision by the court. Conspicuous terms include the following:
9 (i) a heading in capitals equal to or greater in size than the surrounding text, or in contrasting type,
10 font, or color to the surrounding text of the same or lesser size; and
11 (ii) language in the body of a record or display in larger type than the surrounding text, or in
12 contrasting type, font, or color to the surrounding text of the same size, or set off from surrounding text of the
13 same size by symbols or other marks that call attention to the language.
14 (l) (k) "Consumer" means an individual who enters into a transaction primarily for personal, family, or
15 household purposes.
16 (m) (l) "Contract" means the total legal obligation that results from the parties' agreement as affected
17 by this code and as supplemented by any other applicable rules of law.
18 (n) (m) "Creditor" includes a general creditor, a secured creditor, a lien creditor, and any representative
19 of creditors, including an assignee for the benefit of creditors, a trustee in bankruptcy, a receiver in equity, and
20 an executor or administrator of an insolvent debtor's or assignor's estate.
21 (o) (n) "Defendant" includes a person in the position of defendant in a counterclaim or third-party
22 claim.
23 (p) (o) "Delivery" with respect to an electronic document of title means voluntary transfer of control
24 and, with respect to instruments, tangible documents of title, or an instrument, a tangible document of title, or
25 an authoritative tangible copy of a record evidencing chattel paper, means voluntary transfer of possession.
26 (q) (p) (i) "Document of title" means a record:
27 (A) that in the regular course of business or financing is treated as adequately evidencing that the
28 person in possession or control of the record is entitled to receive, control, hold, and dispose of the record and
- 4 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426

****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 the goods the record covers; and
2 (B) that purports to be issued by or addressed to a bailee and to cover goods in the bailee's
3 possession which are either identified or are fungible portions of an identified mass.
4 (ii) The term includes a bill of lading, transport document, dock warrant, dock receipt, warehouse
5 receipt, and order for delivery of goods. An electronic document of title is evidenced by a record consisting of
6 information stored in an electronic medium. A tangible document of title is evidenced by a record consisting of
7 information that is inscribed on a tangible medium.
8 (q) “Electronic” means relating to technology having electrical, digital, magnetic, wireless, optical,
9 electromagnetic, or similar capabilities.
10 (r) "Fault" means wrongful act, omission, breach, or default.
11 (s) "Fungible goods" means:
12 (i) goods of which any unit, by nature or usage of trade, is the equivalent of any other like unit; or
13 (ii) goods which by agreement are treated as equivalent.
14 (t) "Genuine" means free of forgery or counterfeiting.
15 (u) "Good faith", except as otherwise provided in chapter 5, means honesty in fact and the
16 observance of reasonable commercial standards of fair dealing.
17 (v) "Holder" means:
18 (i) the person in possession of a negotiable instrument that is payable either to bearer or to an
19 identified person that is the person in possession;
20 (ii) a the person in possession of a negotiable tangible document of title if the goods are
21 deliverable either to bearer or to the order of the person in possession; or
22 (iii) a the person in control, other than pursuant to 30-7-107(7) of a negotiable electronic document
23 of title.

- 9 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426

****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 401). A "present sale" means a sale which is accomplished by the making of the contract.
2 (2) Goods or conduct including any part of a performance are "conforming" or conform to the
3 contract when they are in accordance with the obligations under the contract.
4 (3) "Termination" occurs when either party pursuant to a power created by agreement or law puts
5 an end to the contract otherwise than for its breach. On "termination" all obligations which are still executory on
6 both sides are discharged but any right based on prior breach or performance survives.
7 (4) "Cancellation" occurs when either party puts an end to the contract for breach by the other and
8 its effect is the same as that of "termination" except that the canceling party also retains any remedy for breach
9 of the whole contract or any unperformed balance.

13 been intended also as a complete and exclusive statement of the terms of the agreement."

8 Section 22. Section 30-3-104, MCA, is amended to read:
9 "30-3-104. Negotiable instrument. (1) "Negotiable instrument" means an unconditional promise or
10 order to pay a fixed amount of money, with or without interest or other charges described in the promise or
11 order, if it:
12 (a) is payable to bearer or to order at the time it is issued or first comes into possession of a
13 holder;
14 (b) is payable on demand or at a definite time; and
15 (c) does not state any other undertaking or instruction by the person promising or ordering
16 payment to do any act in addition to the payment of money except that the promise or order may contain:
17 (i) an undertaking or power to give, maintain, or protect collateral to secure payment;
18 (ii) an authorization or power to the holder to confess judgment or realize on or dispose of
19 collateral; or
20 (iii) a waiver of the benefit of any law intended for the advantage or protection of any obligor;
21 (iv) a term that specifies the law that governs the promise or order; or
22 (v) an undertaking to resolve in a specified forum a dispute concerning the promise or order.
23 (2) "Instrument" means a negotiable instrument.
24 (3) An order that meets all of the requirements of subsection (1) except subsection (1)(a) and
25 otherwise falls within the definition of "check" in subsection (6) is a negotiable instrument and a check.
26 (4) Notwithstanding the provisions of subsection (1), a promise or order other than a check is not
27 an instrument if, at the time it is issued or first comes into possession of a holder, it contains a conspicuous
28 statement, however expressed, indicating that the writing is not an instrument governed by this chapter.

5 Section 26. Section 30-4A-103, MCA, is amended to read:
6 "30-4A-103. Payment order -- definitions. (1) In this chapter, the following definitions apply:
7 (a) "Payment order" means an instruction of a sender to a receiving bank, transmitted orally,
8 electronically, or in writing or in a record, to pay, or to cause another bank to pay, a fixed or determinable
9 amount of money to a beneficiary if:
10 (i) the instruction does not state a condition to payment to the beneficiary other than time of
11 payment;
12 (ii) the receiving bank is to be reimbursed by debiting an account of, or otherwise receiving
13 payment from, the sender; and
14 (iii) the instruction is transmitted by the sender directly to the receiving bank or to an agent, funds-
15 transfer system, or communication system for transmittal to the receiving bank.
16 (b) "Beneficiary" means the person to be paid by the beneficiary's bank.
17 (c) "Beneficiary's bank" means the bank identified in a payment order in which an account of the
18 beneficiary is to be credited pursuant to the order or that otherwise is to make payment to the beneficiary if the
19 order does not provide for payment to an account.
20 (d) "Receiving bank" means the bank to which the sender's instruction is addressed.
21 (e) "Sender" means the person giving the instruction to the receiving bank.
22 (2) If an instruction complying with subsection (1)(a) is to make more than one payment to a
23 beneficiary, the instruction is a separate payment order with respect to each payment.
24 (3) A payment order is issued when it is sent to the receiving bank."

17 Section 28. Section 30-4A-201, MCA, is amended to read:
18 "30-4A-201. Security procedure. "Security procedure" means a procedure established by agreement
19 of a customer and a receiving bank for the purpose of verifying that a payment order or communication
20 amending or canceling a payment order is that of the customer or detecting error in the transmission or the
21 content of the payment order or communication. A security procedure may impose an obligation on the
22 receiving bank or the customer and may require the use of algorithms or other codes, identifying words, or
23 numbers, symbols, sounds, biometrics, encryption, callback procedures, or similar security devices.
24 Comparison of a signature on a payment order or communication with an authorized specimen signature of the
25 customer or requiring a payment order to be sent from a known e-mail address, IP address, or telephone
26 number is not by itself a security procedure."

28 Section 29. Section 30-4A-202, MCA, is amended to read:
- 28 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426

****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 "30-4A-202. Authorized and verified payment orders. (1) A payment order received by the
2 receiving bank is the authorized order of the person identified as sender if that person authorized the order or is
3 otherwise bound by it under the law of agency.
4 (2) If a bank and its customer have agreed that the authenticity of payment orders issued to the
5 bank in the name of the customer as sender will be verified pursuant to a security procedure, a payment order
6 received by the receiving bank is effective as the order of the customer, whether or not authorized, if the
7 security procedure is a commercially reasonable method of providing security against unauthorized payment
8 orders and the bank proves that it accepted the payment order in good faith and in compliance with the bank's
9 obligations under the security procedure and any written agreement or instruction of the customer, evidenced
10 by a record, restricting acceptance of payment orders issued in the name of the customer. The bank is not
11 required to follow an instruction that violates a written an agreement with the customer, evidenced by a record,
12 or notice of which is not received at a time and in a manner affording the bank a reasonable opportunity to act
13 on it before the payment order is accepted.
14 (3) Commercial reasonableness of a security procedure is a question of law to be determined by
15 considering the wishes of the customer expressed to the bank, the circumstances of the customer known to the
16 bank, including the size, type, and frequency of payment orders normally issued by the customer to the bank,
17 alternative security procedures offered to the customer, and security procedures in general use by customers
18 and receiving banks similarly situated. A security procedure is considered to be commercially reasonable if:
19 (a) the security procedure was chosen by the customer after the bank offered, and the customer
20 refused, a security procedure that was commercially reasonable for that customer; and
21 (b) the customer expressly agreed in writing a record to be bound by any payment order, whether
22 or not authorized, issued in the customer's name and accepted by the bank in compliance with the bank's
23 obligation under the security procedure chosen by the customer.
24 (4) The term "sender" in this chapter includes the customer in whose name a payment order is
25 issued if the order is the authorized order of the customer under subsection (1) or if it is effective as the order of
26 the customer under subsection (2).
27 (5) This section applies to amendments and cancellations of payment orders to the same extent it
28 applies to payment orders.

1 (6) Except as provided in this section and in 30-4A-203(1)(a), rights and obligations arising under

- 30 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426

****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (3), if the beneficiary's bank does not know that the

5 Section 33. Section 30-4A-210, MCA, is amended to read:
6 "30-4A-210. Rejection of payment order. (1) A payment order is rejected by the receiving bank by a
7 notice of rejection transmitted to the sender orally, electronically, or in writing a record. A notice of rejection
8 need not use any particular words and is sufficient if it indicates that the receiving bank is rejecting the order or
9 will not execute or pay the order. Rejection is effective when the notice is given if transmission is by a means
10 that is reasonable in the circumstances. If notice of rejection is given by a means that is not reasonable,
11 rejection is effective when the notice is received. If an agreement of the sender and receiving bank establishes
12 the means to be used to reject a payment order:
13 (a) any means complying with the agreement is reasonable; and
14 (b) any means not complying is not reasonable unless no significant delay in receipt of the notice
15 resulted from the use of the noncomplying means.
16 (2) This subsection applies if a receiving bank other than the beneficiary's bank fails to execute a
17 payment order despite the existence on the execution date of a withdrawable credit balance in an authorized
18 account of the sender sufficient to cover the order. If the sender does not receive notice of rejection of the order
19 on the execution date and the authorized account of the sender does not bear interest, the bank is obliged to
20 pay interest to the sender on the amount of the order for the number of days elapsing after the execution date
21 to the earlier of the day the order is canceled pursuant to 30-4A-211(4) or the day the sender receives notice or
22 learns that the order was not executed, counting the final day of the period as an elapsed day. If the
23 withdrawable credit balance during that period falls below the amount of the order, the amount of interest is
24 reduced accordingly.
25 (3) If a receiving bank suspends payments, all unaccepted payment orders issued to it are
26 considered rejected at the time the bank suspends payments.
27 (4) Acceptance of a payment order precludes a later rejection of the order. Rejection of a payment
28 order precludes a later acceptance of the order."

27 losses, to the extent not covered by subsection (1), resulting from the improper execution. Except as provided

20 the document was most recently transferred;

11 Section 41. Section 30-8-113, MCA, is amended to read:
12 "30-8-113. Rules for determining whether certain obligations and interests are securities or
13 financial assets. (1) A share or similar equity interest issued by a corporation, business trust, joint-stock
14 company, or similar entity is a security.
15 (2) An "investment company security" is a security. "Investment company security" means a share
16 or similar equity interest issued by an entity that is registered as an investment company under the federal
17 investment company laws, an interest in a unit investment trust that is so registered, or a face-amount
18 certificate issued by a face-amount certificate company that is so registered. Investment company security does
19 not include an insurance policy or endowment policy or annuity contract issued by an insurance company.
20 (3) An interest in a partnership or limited liability company is not a security unless it is dealt in or
21 traded on securities exchanges or in securities markets, its terms expressly provide that it is a security
22 governed by this chapter, or it is an investment company security. However, an interest in a partnership or
23 limited liability company is a financial asset if it is held in a securities account.
24 (4) A writing that is a security certificate is governed by this chapter and not by chapter 3, even
25 though it also meets the requirements of that chapter. However, a negotiable instrument governed by chapter 3
26 is a financial asset if it is held in a securities account.
27 (5) An option or similar obligation issued by a clearing corporation to its participants is not a
28 security, but is a financial asset.

8 jurisdiction is the jurisdiction in which the chief executive office of the securities intermediary is located.
9 (6) A securities intermediary's jurisdiction is not determined by the physical location of certificates
10 representing financial assets, or by the jurisdiction in which is organized the issuer of the financial asset with
11 respect to which an entitlement holder has a security entitlement, or by the location of facilities for data
12 processing or other recordkeeping concerning the account.
13 (7) The local law of the issuer’s jurisdiction or the securities intermediary’s jurisdiction governs a
14 matter or transaction specified in subsection (1) or (2) even if the matter or transaction does not bear any
15 relation to the jurisdiction."
16
17 Section 44. Section 30-8-333, MCA, is amended to read:
18 "30-8-333. Protected purchaser. (1) "Protected purchaser" means a purchaser of a certificated or
19 uncertificated security, or of an interest therein, who:
20 (a) gives value;
21 (b) does not have notice of any adverse claim to the security; and
22 (c) obtains control of the certificated or uncertificated security.
23 (2) In addition to acquiring the rights of a purchaser, a A protected purchaser also acquires its
24 interest in the security free of any adverse claim."

2 in a particular jurisdiction, that jurisdiction is the bank's jurisdiction.

4 office identified in an account statement as the office serving the customer's account is located.
5 (e) If none of the preceding subsections apply, the bank's jurisdiction is the jurisdiction in which the
6 chief executive office of the bank is located."

19 NEW SECTION. Section 59. Laws governing perfection and priority of security interests in
20 chattel paper. (1) Except as provided in subsection (4), if chattel paper is evidenced only by an authoritative
21 electronic copy of the chattel paper or is evidenced by an authoritative electronic copy and an authoritative
22 tangible copy, the local law of the chattel paper’s jurisdiction governs perfection, the effect of perfection or
23 nonperfection, and the priority of a security interest in the chattel paper, even if the transaction does not bear
24 any relation to the chattel paper’s jurisdiction.
25 (2) The following rules determine the chattel paper’s jurisdiction under this section:
26 (a) If the authoritative electronic copy of the record evidencing chattel paper, or a record attached
27 to or logically associated with the electronic copy and readily available for review, expressly provides that a
28 particular jurisdiction is the chattel paper’s jurisdiction for purposes of this part, this chapter, or this code, that
- 78 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426

****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 jurisdiction is the chattel paper’s jurisdiction.
2 (b) If subsection (2)(a) does not apply and the rules of the system in which the authoritative
3 electronic copy is recorded are readily available for review and expressly provide that a particular jurisdiction is
4 the chattel paper’s jurisdiction for purposes of this part, this chapter, or this code, that jurisdiction is the chattel
5 paper’s jurisdiction.
6 (c) If subsections (2)(a) and (2)(b) do not apply and the authoritative electronic copy, or a record
7 attached to or logically associated with the electronic copy and readily available for review, expressly provides
8 that the chattel paper is governed by the law of a particular jurisdiction, that jurisdiction is the chattel paper’s
9 jurisdiction.
10 (d) If subsections (2)(a), (2)(b), and (2)(c) do not apply and the rules of the system in which the
11 authoritative electronic copy is recorded are readily available for review and expressly provide that the chattel
12 paper or the system is governed by the law of a particular jurisdiction, that jurisdiction is the chattel paper’s
13 jurisdiction.
14 (e) If subsections (2)(a) through (2)(d) do not apply, the chattel paper’s jurisdiction is the
15 jurisdiction in which the debtor is located.
16 (3) If an authoritative tangible copy of a record evidences chattel paper and the chattel paper is not
17 evidenced by an authoritative electronic copy, while the authoritative tangible copy of the record evidencing
18 chattel paper is located in a jurisdiction, the local law of that jurisdiction governs:

20 (b) the effect of perfection or nonperfection and the priority of a security interest in the chattel
21 paper.

23 interest in chattel paper by filing.

11 NEW SECTION. Section 70. Priority of security interest in controllable account, controllable
12 electronic record, and controllable payment intangible. A security interest in a controllable account,
13 controllable electronic record, or controllable payment intangible held by a secured party having control of the
14 account, electronic record, or payment intangible has priority over a conflicting security interest held by a
15 secured party that does not have control.

17 proceeds is completed.

19 furnish reasonable proof of the interest or lien within a reasonable time. Unless the holder complies, the
20 secured party need not comply with the holder's demand under subsection (1)(a)(iii).
21 (c) A secured party need not apply or pay over for application the noncash proceeds of collection
22 and enforcement under 30-9A-607 unless the failure to do so would be commercially unreasonable. A secured
23 party that applies or pays over for application noncash proceeds shall do so in a commercially reasonable
24 manner.
25 (d) A secured party shall account to and pay a debtor for any surplus, and the obligor is liable for
26 any deficiency.

28 promissory notes, the debtor is not entitled to any surplus and the obligor is not liable for any deficiency."

11 Section 85. Section 30-9A-613, MCA, is amended to read:
12 "30-9A-613. Contents and form of notification before disposition of collateral -- general. (1)
13 Except in a consumer-goods transaction, the following rules apply:
14 (a) The contents of a notification of disposition are sufficient if the notification:
15 (i) describes the debtor and the secured party;
16 (ii) describes the collateral that is the subject of the intended disposition;
17 (iii) states the method of intended disposition;
18 (iv) states that the debtor is entitled to an accounting of the unpaid indebtedness and states the
19 charge, if any, for an accounting; and
20 (v) states the time and place of a public disposition or the time after which any other disposition is
21 to be made.
22 (b) Whether the contents of a notification that lacks any of the information set forth in subsection
23 (1) are nevertheless sufficient is a question of fact.
24 (c) The contents of a notification providing substantially the information specified in subsection (1)
25 are sufficient, even if the notification includes:
26 (i) information not specified by that subsection; or
27 (ii) minor errors that are not seriously misleading.
28 (d) A particular phrasing of the notification is not required.

2 NEW SECTION. Section 95. Definitions. (1) As used in [sections 94 through 100], the following
3 definitions apply:
4 (a) (i) “Controllable electronic record” means a record stored in an electronic medium that can be
5 subjected to control under [section 98].
6 (ii) The term does not include a controllable account, a controllable payment intangible, a deposit
7 account, an electronic copy of a record evidencing chattel paper, an electronic document of title, investment
8 property, a transferable record, or an electronic record that is currently authorized or adopted by a domestic or
9 foreign government and is not a medium of exchange that was recorded and transferable in a system that
10 existed and operated for the medium of exchange before the medium of exchange was authorized or adopted
11 by a government.
12 (b) “Qualifying purchaser” means a purchaser of a controllable electronic record or an interest in a
13 controllable electronic record that obtains control of the controllable electronic record for value, in good faith,
14 and without notice of a claim of a property right in the controllable electronic record.
15 (c) “Transferable record” has the meaning provided for that term in:
16 (i) Section 201(a)(1) of the Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act, 15 U.S.C.
17 Section 7021(a)(1); or
18 (ii) 30-18-115(1).
19 (d) “Value” has the meaning provided in 30-3-303(1), as if references in that subsection to an
20 “instrument” were references to a controllable account, controllable electronic record, or controllable payment
21 intangible.
22 (2) The definitions in Title 30, chapter 9A, of “account debtor”, “controllable account”, “controllable
23 payment intangible”, “chattel paper”, “deposit account”, and “investment property” apply to [sections 94 through
24 100].
25 (3) Title 30, chapter 1, contains general definitions and principles of construction and interpretation
26 applicable throughout [sections 94 through 100].

6 NEW SECTION. Section 97. Rights in controllable account, controllable electronic record, and
7 controllable payment intangible. (1) This section applies to the acquisition and purchase of rights in a
8 controllable account or controllable payment intangible, including the rights and benefits under subsections (3),
9 (4), (5), (7), and (8) of a purchaser and qualifying purchaser, in the same manner this section applies to a
10 controllable electronic record.
11 (2) To determine whether a purchaser of a controllable account or a controllable payment
12 intangible is a qualifying purchaser, the purchaser obtains control of the account or payment intangible if it
13 obtains control of the controllable electronic record that evidences the account or payment intangible.
14 (3) Except as provided in this section, law other than [sections 94 through 100] determines
15 whether a person acquires a right in a controllable electronic record and the right the person acquires.
16 (4) A purchaser of a controllable electronic record acquires all rights in the controllable electronic
17 record that the transferor had or had power to transfer, except that a purchaser of a limited interest in a
18 controllable electronic record acquires rights only to the extent of the interest purchased.
19 (5) A qualifying purchaser acquires its rights in the controllable electronic record free of a claim of
20 a property right in the controllable electronic record.
21 (6) Except as provided in subsections (1) and (5) for a controllable account and a controllable
22 payment intangible or law other than [sections 94 through 100], a qualifying purchaser takes a right to payment,
23 right to performance, or other interest in property evidenced by the controllable electronic record subject to a
24 claim of a property right in the right to payment, right to performance, or other interest in property.
25 (7) An action may not be asserted against a qualifying purchaser based on both a purchase by the
26 qualifying purchaser of a controllable electronic record and a claim of a property right in another controllable
27 electronic record, whether the action is framed in conversion, replevin, constructive trust, equitable lien, or other
28 theory.

****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 (8) Filing of a financing statement under Title 30, chapter 9A, is not notice of a claim of a property
2 right in a controllable electronic record.

4 NEW SECTION. Section 98. Control of controllable electronic record. (1) A person has control of
5 a controllable electronic record if the electronic record, a record attached to or logically associated with the
6 electronic record, or a system in which the electronic record is recorded:
7 (a) gives the person:
8 (i) power to avail itself of substantially all the benefit from the electronic record; and
9 (ii) exclusive power, subject to subsection (2), to:
10 (A) prevent others from availing themselves of substantially all the benefit from the electronic
11 record; and
12 (B) transfer control of the electronic record to another person or cause another person to obtain
13 control of another controllable electronic record as a result of the transfer of the electronic record; and
14 (b) enables the person readily to identify itself in any way, including by name, identifying number,
15 cryptographic key, office, or account number, as having the powers specified in subjection (1)(a).
16 (2) Subject to subsection (3), a power is exclusive under subsection (1)(a)(ii)(A) and (1)(a)(ii)(B)
17 even if:
18 (a) the controllable electronic record, a record attached to or logically associated with the
19 electronic record, or a system in which the electronic record is recorded limits the use of the electronic record or
20 has a protocol programmed to cause a change, including a transfer or loss of control or a modification of
21 benefits afforded by the electronic record; or
22 (b) the power is shared with another person.
23 (3) A power of a person is not shared with another person under subsection (2)(b) and the
24 person’s power is not exclusive if:
25 (a) the person can exercise the power only if the power also is exercised by the other person; and
26 (b) the other person:
27 (i) can exercise the power without exercise of the power by the person; or
28 (ii) is the transferor to the person of an interest in the controllable electronic record or a
- 124 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426

****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 controllable account or controllable payment intangible evidenced by the controllable electronic record.
2 (4) If a person has the powers specified in subsections (1)(a)(ii)(A) and (1)(a)(ii)(B), the powers are
3 presumed to be exclusive.
4 (5) A person has control of a controllable electronic record if another person, other than the
5 transferor to the person of an interest in the controllable electronic record or a controllable account or
6 controllable payment intangible evidenced by the controllable electronic record:
7 (a) has control of the electronic record and acknowledges that it has control on behalf of the
8 person; or
9 (b) obtains control of the electronic record after having acknowledged that it will obtain control of
10 the electronic record on behalf of the person.
11 (6) A person that has control under this section is not required to acknowledge that it has control
12 on behalf of another person.
13 (7) If a person acknowledges that it has or will obtain control on behalf of another person, unless
14 the person otherwise agrees or a law other than Title 30, chapter 9A, or [sections 94 through 100] otherwise
15 provides, the person does not owe any duty to the other person and is not required to confirm the
16 acknowledgment to any other person.
17
18 NEW SECTION. Section 99. Discharge of account debtor on controllable account or
19 controllable payment intangible. (1) An account debtor on a controllable account or controllable payment
20 intangible may discharge its obligation by paying:
21 (a) the person having control of the controllable electronic record that evidences the controllable
22 account or controllable payment intangible; or
23 (b) except as provided in subsection (2), a person that formerly had control of the controllable
24 electronic record.
25 (2) Subject to subsection (4), the account debtor may not discharge its obligation by paying a
26 person that formerly had control of the controllable electronic record if the account debtor receives a notification
27 that:
28 (a) is signed by a person that formerly had control or the person to which control was transferred;
- 125 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426

****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 (b) reasonably identifies the controllable account or controllable payment intangible;
2 (c) notifies the account debtor that control of the controllable electronic record that evidences the
3 controllable account or controllable payment intangible was transferred;
4 (d) identifies the transferee, in any reasonable way, including by name, identifying number,
5 cryptographic key, office, or account number; and
6 (e) provides a commercially reasonable method by which the account debtor is to pay the
7 transferee.
8 (3) After receipt of a notification that complies with subsection (2), the account debtor may
9 discharge its obligation by paying in accordance with the notification and may not discharge the obligation by
10 paying a person that formerly had control.
11 (4) Subject to subsection (8), notification is ineffective under subsection (2):
12 (a) unless, before the notification is sent, the account debtor and the person that, at that time, had
13 control of the controllable electronic record that evidences the controllable account or controllable payment
14 intangible agree in a signed record to a commercially reasonable method by which a person may furnish
15 reasonable proof that control has been transferred;
16 (b) to the extent an agreement between the account debtor and seller of a payment intangible
17 limits the account debtor’s duty to pay a person other than the seller and the limitation is effective under law
18 other than [sections 94 through 100]; or

20 (i) divide a payment;
21 (ii) make less than the full amount of an installment or other periodic payment; or
22 (iii) pay any part of a payment by more than one method or to more than one person.
23 (5) Subject to subsection (8), if requested by the account debtor, the person giving the notification
24 under subsection (2) seasonably shall furnish reasonable proof, using the method in the agreement referred to
25 in subsection (4)(a), that control of the controllable electronic record has been transferred. Unless the person
26 complies with the request, the account debtor may discharge its obligation by paying a person that formerly had
27 control, even if the account debtor has received a notification under subsection (2).
28 (6) A person furnishes reasonable proof under subsection (5) that control has been transferred if
- 126 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426

****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 the person demonstrates, using the method in the agreement referred to in subsection (4)(a), that the
2 transferee has the power to:

4 (b) prevent others from availing themselves of substantially all the benefit from the controllable
5 electronic record; and
6 (c) transfer the powers specified in subsections (6)(a) and (6)(b) to another person.

13 NEW SECTION. Section 100. Governing law. (1) (1) Except as provided in subsection (2), the local
14 law of a controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction governs a matter covered by [sections 94 through 100].
15 (2) For a controllable electronic record that evidences a controllable account or controllable
16 payment intangible, the local law of the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction governs a matter covered by
17 [section 99] unless an effective agreement determines that the local law of another jurisdiction governs.
18 (3) The following rules determine a controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction under this section:
19 (a) If the controllable electronic record, or a record attached to or logically associated with the
20 controllable electronic record and readily available for review, expressly provides that a particular jurisdiction is
21 the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction for purposes of this code or [sections 94 through 100], that
22 jurisdiction is the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction.
23 (b) If subsection (3)(a) does not apply and the rules of the system in which the controllable
24 electronic record is recorded are readily available for review and expressly provide that a particular jurisdiction
25 is the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction for purposes of this code or [sections 94 through 100], that
26 jurisdiction is the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction.
27 (c) If subsections (3)(a) and (3)(b) do not apply and the controllable electronic record, or a record
28 attached to or logically associated with the controllable electronic record and readily available for review,
- 127 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426

****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 expressly provides that the controllable electronic record is governed by the law of a particular jurisdiction, that
2 jurisdiction is the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction.
3 (d) If subsections (3)(a) through (3)(c) do not apply and the rules of the system in which the
4 controllable electronic record is recorded are readily available for review and expressly provide that the
5 controllable electronic record or the system is governed by the law of a particular jurisdiction, that jurisdiction is
6 the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction.
7 (e) If subsections (3)(a) through (3)(d) do not apply, the controllable electronic record’s jurisdiction
8 is the District of Columbia.
9 (4) (a) If subsection (3)(e) applies and [sections 94 through 100] are not in effect in the District of
10 Columbia without material modification, the governing law for a matter covered by [sections 94 through 100] is
11 the law of the District of Columbia as though [sections 94 through 100] were in effect in the District of Columbia
12 without material modification.
13 (b) In this subsection (4), “[sections 94 through 100]" means Article 12 of Uniform Commercial
14 Code Amendments (2022).
15 (5) To the extent subsections (1) and (2) provide that the local law of the controllable electronic
16 record’s jurisdiction governs a matter covered by [sections 94 through 100], that law governs even if the matter
17 or a transaction to which the matter relates does not bear any relation to the controllable electronic record’s
18 jurisdiction.
19 (6) The rights acquired under [section 95] by a purchaser or qualifying purchaser are governed by
20 the law applicable under this section at the time of purchase.

11 act], but the requirements for enforceability or perfection under [this act] are not satisfied on [the effective date
12 of this act], the security interest:
13 (a) is a perfected security interest until the earlier of the time perfection would have ceased under
14 the law in effect immediately before [the effective date of this act] or the adjustment date;
15 (b) remains enforceable thereafter only if the security interest satisfies the requirements for
16 enforceability under 30-9A-203, as amended by [this act], before the adjustment date; and
17 (c) remains perfected thereafter only if the requirements for perfection under [this act] are satisfied
18 before the time specified in subsection (2)(a).

6 effective date of this act], the action is effective to perfect a security interest that attaches under [this act] before

8 security interest becomes a perfected security interest under [this act] before the adjustment date.

10 security interest on [the effective date of this act] to the extent the filing would satisfy the requirements for
11 perfection under [this act].

13 a security interest on [the effective date of this act] if the action would satisfy the requirements for enforceability
14 under [this act].

6 chapter.
7 (3) The agricultural lien statement must be in the form prescribed by the secretary of state.
8 (4) The secretary of state shall:
9 (a) record the agricultural lien statement on the centralized computer system as set forth in 30-9A-
10 501; and
11 (b) establish fees for such recordings as set forth in 30-9A-525.
12 (5) For the purposes of this section, an agricultural lien means a lien under part 4, 7, 8, or 9 of this
13 chapter.
14 (6) A statement of an agricultural lien or continuation statement that has been filed at the office of
15 the county clerk and recorder lapses on March 31, 1990, unless prior to that date there is filed in the office of
16 the secretary of state a certified copy of the statement and all related documents on file with the county clerk
17 and recorder."
18
19 NEW SECTION. Section 111. Central bank digital currency -- approval by state. As applicable in
20 this state, the term "money" does not include any central bank digital currency or any requirement to accept or
21 use a central bank digital currency, unless the central bank digital currency is specifically recognized and
22 approved by Montana law.
23
24 NEW SECTION. Section 112. Codification instruction. (1) [Section 48] is intended to be codified as
25 30-9A-107A, and the provisions of Title 30, chapters 1 through 9A, apply to [section 48].
26 (2) [Section 49] is intended to be codified as 30-9A-107B, and the provisions of Title 30, chapters 1
27 through 9A, apply to [section 49].
28 (3) [Section 59] is intended to be codified as 30-9A-306A, and the provisions of Title 30, chapters 1
- 133 - Authorized Print Version – SB 426

****
69th Legislature 2025 SB 426.1
1 through 9A, apply to [section 59].
2 (4) [Section 60] is intended to be codified as 30-9A-306B, and the provisions of Title 30, chapters 1
3 through 9A, apply to [section 60].
4 (5) [Section 65] is intended to be codified as 30-9A-314A, and the provisions of Title 30, chapters 1
5 through 9A, apply to [section 65].
6 (6) [Section 70] is intended to be codified as 30-9A-326A, and the provisions of Title 30, chapters 1
7 through 9A, apply to [section 70].
8 (7) [Sections 94 through 100] are intended to be codified as a new part in Title 30, chapter 12A,
9 and the provisions of Title 30, chapters 1 through 9A, apply to [sections 94 through 100].
10 (8) [Sections 101 through 109] are intended to be codified as a new part in Title 30, chapter 12A,
11 and the provisions of Title 30, chapters 1 through 9A, apply to [sections 101 through 109].
12 (9) [Sections 102 through 107] are intended to be codified as a new part in Title 30, chapter 9A,
13 and the provisions of Title 30, chapters 1 through 9A, apply to [sections 102 through 107].
14 (10) [Section 110] is intended to be codified as a new part in Title 30, chapter 14, and the provisions
15 of Title 30, chapter 14, apply to [section 110].
16
17 NEW SECTION. Section 113. Directions to code commissioner. The code commissioner is
18 instructed to strike the reference to "tangible chattel paper" in 30-9A-338(2).
19
20 NEW SECTION. Section 114. Severability. If a part of [this act] is invalid, all valid parts that are
21 severable from the invalid part remain in effect. If a part of [this act] is invalid in one or more of its applications,
22 the part remains in effect in all valid applications that are severable from the invalid applications.
23 - END -
